Songjiang 88

Unauthorized Engraving of Official Seals Discovered and Thoroughly Investigated. On the 18th, a person named Jiang Anren sent someone to Gu Wenbao Qike Zipu in Xicheng with a sample and asked him to engrave two seals: "Songjiang County Education Bureau Seal" and the bureau chief's "Ni Han Chen Seal." He also asked him to engrave three seals for the Songjiang County Education Mistake Seal, and asked him to wrap them up and send them by 6:00 p.m. The Education Bureau noticed the matter and suspected Jiang Anren of the crime of unauthorized engraving of official seals. It immediately reported it to the Public Security Bureau, which sent police to arrest Jiang. Director Yu of the branch office held a preliminary trial. Jiang's confession seemed to be neurological, and his attitude was abnormal. Yu ordered him to be handed over to the county government for review. Jiang was temporarily released on bail that night. It is found that Jiang Anren is currently an executive member of the County Education Association, the town chief of Guyang, and a teacher at the Second High School. During the recent turmoil at the Second High School, he was at the forefront of the student movement. He recently returned to Songjiang from Zhenjiang and told others that he had met with Director Chen of the Department of Education and discussed the education of Songjiang in detail. It is unknown what kind of stimulus he received, but he suddenly suffered a nervous breakdown and went beyond the scope, committing the act of unauthorized engraving of official seals. The Public Security Bureau has now handed over the case to the county for legal resolution.

Joint Meeting of Three Counties on Defense Matters. Hu Mingzao, the head of the First Regiment of the Anti-Smuggling Office stationed in Songjiang, is responsible for guarding the special affairs of Songjiang, Jinshan, and Qing counties. He convened a joint meeting of the three counties on the 18th. Head Hu chaired the meeting and reported on the intention of the meeting. The discussion was that the investigation of bandits in the three counties should be the responsibility of the county magistrates, who should instruct the Public Security Bureaus to be responsible for handling the matter, and the Public Security Bureaus should send a detective to be stationed at the headquarters to await dispatch. The northern section of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway should be the responsibility of the police chief or station chief of that section, who should instruct the patrol officers to report at any time. If bandits are found in one county, other counties should be on alert at the same time and provide assistance. The transportation undertakings in each county should be maintained by the Public Security Bureau of that county, and the garrison troops in the location should be responsible for assisting. The officers and soldiers of this regiment who are swaggering outside or behaving irregularly must be apprehended or reported for rectification. Each county magistrate should conduct a thorough investigation and report on the public and private armed groups within their jurisdiction.

Bandits Apprehended and Sent for Trial in the Five Warehouse Robbery Case. The Shen Yuan Gu family of Wuku Thirty-four Tu was robbed on June 28th. Shen, a patrol officer of the township, has apprehended Zhu Awu, a resident of this town, who confessed to robbing the Shen family. He has been handed over to the County Public Security Bureau and then to the County Government for legal action.

Suzhou 90

The Truth About the Arrest of Communists: In the case of Suzhou arresting communists, this newspaper has already given a brief account. It is now known that this matter began on the 16th of this month when postal inspectors at the Changmen Wai post office intercepted a bundle of reactionary publications addressed to Wei Junhong of Le Yi Girls' School for forwarding to Wu Shijie. This was reported to party and government personnel, who, together with the police, went directly to Le Yi at Wang Feiji. There, they found only the administrative director, Wei Pi. After repeated questioning, they learned that Junhong was Wei Pi's real name. According to his confession, he had received such printed materials several times before and had handed them over to Jiang Weixi. He himself had once opened and read one. Jiang was a classmate from when he attended the county junior high school and is now studying at a certain middle school in Shanghai. Because of the summer vacation, he was also residing at Le Yi. When Jiang was questioned, he said that he had an old acquaintance with Cai Zhihua and that after the reactionary publications were sent to Suzhou, Cai would always get them from Wei. He also said that Cai would be coming that day to pick up a letter. A search of Jiang's person yielded a page of unsigned stationery; the envelope had already been destroyed. The party and government personnel searching the school then took Wei and Jiang to the Public Security Bureau and then went to No. 1 Chuanfang Lane, where they arrested Cai Zhihua. At the same time, near Canglang Pavilion, they arrested a female student who looked suspicious and was carrying multiple reactionary publications. After being taken to the bureau, she identified herself as Yang Zhongxian, 19 years old, from Sichuan, and currently a member of the Zhongshan Physical Education School's Girl Scouts. Subsequently, those arrested confessed to the involvement of Zhang Yimin, Wang Menglu, Ge Naibin, Gu Linfan, and others. The Public Security Bureau conducted separate searches at their addresses. They arrested Zhang Yimin and Ge Naibin at a primary school in the city center. Zhang Chongchun, a teacher at Shen Xiao Primary School, and Ge, a teacher at the school in the city center. They also found dozens of reactionary books at Gu Linfan's home at No. 35 Liu Lane. This is the true story of the case from beginning to end. It is also heard that the party and government authorities yesterday (the 19th) presented the details to the Provincial Rectification Committee for handling, and the Provincial Rectification Committee has scheduled to send personnel to Suzhou within days to investigate and verify.

Furthermore, around 1 AM the previous morning, the Public Security Bureau received a tip that there were many communists holding a secret meeting at the Zhonghua Hotel outside the Changmen gate. After receiving the report, the director ordered dozens of armed police officers to rush to the hotel, surround it, and arrest the main offenders, Wang Guangming and Xu Yuanzhang (native place unknown), along with eighty-eight reactionary flags and numerous symbols. They were immediately detained in the Public Security Bureau. Under preliminary interrogation by the director, they confessed to plotting to seize local military and police firearms and occupy the city of Suzhou.

Yesterday evening, around 8 PM, wounded soldiers caused a disturbance in the city. All city gates were closed, and shops closed down. A guard standing at the Guangji Bridge pier was taken away by the wounded soldiers, and another policeman was severely beaten. The third branch of the Public Security Bureau and the second station were robbed of a sentry gun by the wounded soldiers. It is said that there were more than 300 wounded soldiers. After the incident, the military and police authorities announced temporary martial law and cut off transportation.

Wuxi 91

Mediation Conference on Labor-Management Disputes in Silk Factories: Due to unresolved disputes over revisions to the labor-management contract, Wuxi silk factories have been delayed for a long time. The County Party Rectification Committee, having accepted the requests of both labor and management, and following the instructions of the Provincial Party Committee, originally scheduled a mediation conference for both parties on the 8th of this month. However, due to the management's failure to put forward responsible representatives, it was postponed to the afternoon of the 18th and held at the County Party Rectification Committee. On that day, 45 representatives from all factories on the management side and 23 male and female committee members from the labor side attended. Representatives from the County Government's Labor Rectification Committee and the County Chamber of Commerce also attended. Zhang Renjie, a member of the Public Education Committee, chaired the meeting. He first reported the purpose of the mediation, and then both parties began discussions lasting four hours. The results were as follows: (1) The issue of revising the contract will be resolved by a mediation committee organized by the party and government organs within a short period. (2) Before the new contract is finalized, the original state should be maintained in accordance with the old contract, and wages for memorial days stipulated by the central government should be paid as usual. (3) All factories that went on strike today should resume work uniformly, and the trade union should be responsible for ensuring that there are no more strikes in factories that have not gone on strike. (4) The forced strike of five factories today will be thoroughly investigated by the party and government, and strict action will be taken according to the law. After the above was discussed, the chairman declared that the silk factories' poor business performance was indeed a fact, but the rising cost of living for workers was also difficult. Both parties should act in the spirit of labor-management cooperation, remove prejudices, and make concessions to facilitate a solution. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Homicide and Robbery Case - On-site Investigation: Wang A'de, a migrant living in Shangwen'an Village, Meijing, 16th District (Wan'an), was shot and killed by robbers the previous night while pursuing them. The next day, Chen Genze, a cousin of the deceased, reported the case to the county government and requested an investigation. Yu, an investigator from the county government, led police officers to conduct an on-site investigation. It was found that the deceased had been shot three times, with one bullet entering the left abdomen and exiting through the back, which was the fatal wound. It was also learned that the deceased Wang A'de's family was extremely poor, but they had received a hundred yuan from a hui loan last month, which was coveted by the robbers. However, the money had already been used to pay off debts. The robbers were angered by not finding anything, and because A'de pursued them, he was killed. After questioning, Mr. Yu ordered the family to prepare a coffin and await the arrest of the perpetrators.

Resolution of the Labor Dispute in Five Silk Factories: The five silk factories in Zhou Shanbang, including Deda Yu, Ruichang, Qianfeng, Wan Yi, and Yuanfeng, suddenly experienced a strike at around 6 AM the day before yesterday, and the atmosphere was tense for a time. After this incident occurred, the county government, the county party headquarters, and the county public security bureau all sent teams to suppress the situation and maintain order. Finally, Zhou Fengjing, the leader of the county party headquarters, and Lu Qi, a representative of the county government, did their best to mediate between labor and management, persuading both parties to settle the matter and ensure peace. Representatives of both parties were willing to respect the leaders of the party and government, maintain production increases, and agreed to resume work immediately. Therefore, yesterday morning (the 19th), the female workers of the five factories, including Deda Yu, all resumed work and worked as usual.

Zhenjiang 92

Chamber of Commerce Notice Regarding the Large-Scale Stamp Tax Inspection: The Zhenjiang Stamp Tax Bureau has a customary practice of conducting a large-scale inspection every six months. This inspection period is scheduled for the 21st of this month. In accordance with the regulations, the police will be involved and will seriously start the inspection in the areas under their jurisdiction. The Chamber of Commerce was notified in advance to inform all stores that if there are any items that have not yet been affixed with stamps, they must be affixed in accordance with the regulations to avoid omissions and penalties. After approving the letter, the Chamber of Commerce specifically notified all stores yesterday to pay special attention to avoid misunderstandings occurring temporarily. Establishment of Rice Inspection Offices in Jiangsu Province: In Jiangsu Province, rice is usually allowed to circulate within the province without restrictions. However, private smuggling out of the province and leakage into the sea are prohibited. The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs believes that the rice circulation passports previously issued have many drawbacks, so it has cancelled the passports and formulated new measures to punish rice smuggling and leakage into the sea. The measures have been submitted to the Provincial Committee for discussion and approval, and orders have been issued for compliance. It is now found that the areas along the Yangtze River and the sea in Jiangsu Province and the counties bordering neighboring provinces are vast, making smuggling easy. If special agencies are not set up to seriously inspect and verify, it will be impossible to prevent smuggling and hold people accountable. Therefore, it is stipulated that eight inspection offices should be set up in Shanghai, Wuxi, Tongshan, Donghai, Jiangpu, Yixing, Wujiang, Jiangning, and other counties at important land and water intersections, and that regulations should be formulated and approved for implementation. It is also ordered that all regulations attached to the previous collection of permit fees should be abolished.

Successors to District Chiefs After Training in the Provincial Capital: Eight or nine out of ten district chiefs in various counties have been ordered to go to the provincial capital for training. However, in general, there are still three district chiefs from the second graduating class who have not been able to obtain vacancies to this day. Although the date for passing the selection is still far away, there are many who are planning in advance to fill the above vacancies.

Local Correspondences Two

Qingjiang 97

Villagers Greatly Alarmed: Since the remnants of the Sifeilin Third Division fled to Xiaoying on the evening of the 13th in Huaiyin Third District, although they were forced away by the various joint village self-defense groups, the people's hearts were still uneasy, and there were inevitably rumors from time to time. On the evening of the 15th, before the setting sun had even fallen, the villagers along the northern bank of the Yanhe River, including Shilijing, Shijia Dawang, and the eastern bank of Da Hong, suddenly fled in all directions, supporting the old and carrying the young, as if a great disaster was about to occur. However, there is nothing strange in the world. Coincidentally, on that evening, more than a dozen new soldiers from the Second Division rushed to the Xiaoying Yanhe Ferry. At that time, the pontoon bridge had already been removed, and it was dark. Residents on the opposite bank could not distinguish them. Together with the villagers' flight that afternoon, there were many doubts. Therefore, merchants in Wangying and Xiba towns were especially prepared. In Wangying, the Public Security Corps and the Public Security Bureau派出所 all sent out teams. Xiba was even more prepared, with all of the Salt Defense Camp, Smuggling Suppression Camp, and Salt Transport Escort Team departing to set up outposts in places such as Huihui Ying, Hehua Wang, and Wutiao Road. A machine gun was set up at the intersection of Wutiao Road to prepare for unforeseen circumstances. On the one hand, the merchants of Wangying, seeing that the new soldiers were frequently calling for a ferry, found it difficult to ignore them. They temporarily appointed two representatives to cross the Yanhe River in a small boat to find out what was going on. When they arrived, they saw that the new soldiers had no weapons and were definitely not bandits. They first politely asked them to wait until this morning (the 16th) to cross the river, offering them food and lodging for the night. Seeing that the situation was difficult to refuse, they simultaneously called for a ferry to the south bank, and at that moment, the group's doubts were dispelled.

Former County Magistrate Chen Sends Personnel for Handover: When the former Huaiyin County Magistrate Chen Buchan stepped down, there were still some items in the various accounts he had handled that had not been cleared up. He specifically sent Hu Shaomei with funds to Huaiyin to clear the accounts some days ago. However, Hu brought 1,600 silver dollars from Chen, but after arriving in Pu, he did not hand over the money. The current County Magistrate Xu said that the handover of Chen's term was being urgently urged by the provincial and departmental authorities. Now that Hu has come as Chen's representative, he can be held responsible for clearing the accounts. Therefore, the police were sent to monitor Hu's residence at the Jisheng Society. At the same time, a telegram was still sent to Chen urging him to come quickly to clear the remaining procedures so that the case could be resolved as soon as possible.

Ningbo 98

Conference on the Construction of Iron Gates at Dasong Port: The construction of iron gates at Dasong Port in Yinxian County to block salt and store fresh water is of great importance for the irrigation of farmland in the Daxian area. The Yinxian County Government, together with local people, organized a preparatory committee and elected County Magistrate Chen Baolin and Head of the Construction Section Ni Weixiong as the chairman and vice-chairman. Preparations have been going on for several months. Now that Hu Jianfen, a technician from the county government, has completed the survey and the engineering outline has been drafted, the committee specially convened a standing committee yesterday to discuss the progress of the project and other important issues in order to see its completion as soon as possible. It is heard that the engineering fund is tentatively set at 100,000 yuan, and personnel will be sent to Nantong and Shaoxing to inspect the gate projects in those two places for reference.

Command Headquarters Sends Teams to Vigorously Suppress Pirates: The Command Headquarters for Suppressing Bandits in the four prefectures of Ningbo, Shaoxing, Taizhou, and Wenzhou stationed in this port recently received reports that pirates in the area near Xiangshan Port were colluding with local bandits from various counties to take advantage of the situation. After receiving the report, Commander Wang immediately transferred two marine police detachments and a guerrilla detachment to rush to the area for suppression, together with patrol ships. They suddenly encountered bandits in the Qingzi Port area and immediately engaged in fierce fighting. The Ministry of the Navy, upon hearing the news, also sent the Jinxing gunboat to the waters off Shenjiamen to join forces with the security team of the provincial government to encircle and suppress them. One bandit leader was killed on the spot. The bandits then fled in three routes. Martial law was immediately declared in the Xiangshan Port area. The Zhejiang Customs Supervisory Office also notified the shipping companies operating on the Zhejiang seas to temporarily suspend all coastal merchant ships to avoid accidents. All the suppression troops are currently pursuing and suppressing the bandits separately.

The Black Market for Rice Merchants Manipulates Rice Prices During the Fair Price Sale: Since the local Civil Food Relief Association has been running the fair price sale, the poor have benefited greatly. However, the market price of rice in the city suddenly dropped from sixteen yuan and eight jiao to twelve yuan and eight jiao within the last few days, a sharp drop of four yuan. The Civil Food Association believed that since the price of rice had fallen, it was about to start wrapping up and planned to sell off the remaining rice. Yesterday, someone familiar with the rice industry came to the association and reported that the sharp drop in the price of rice was not a real rise or fall in the price of rice. According to the Shanghai rice price calculation, it should be at least six liang or more, which is difficult to sell at twelve yuan and eight jiao. It was a few unscrupulous merchants who planned to first lower the price of rice so that the Civil Food Association's stored rice could be sold and the fair price sale could be concluded. After achieving their goal, they would then raise the price of rice again. At that time, even if the Civil Food Association could find a way, it would be of little help. These people would then be able to make a big profit. After hearing this report, the Civil Food Association immediately issued a notice overnight to convene an emergency meeting this morning to discuss how to resolve the case.

Shangyu 99

Hurricane Causes Havoc and Kills Three People: Chen Laoyun, a Qiaomin from Taizhou, was 56 years old, his wife Xu was 52 years old, and his son Xunshun was 16 years old. They had been renting a dilapidated house belonging to the Shi family in Xujiatan, Yasaiyan, Yinxian County, for more than a year. At 2 AM on the 15th, the dilapidated house they lived in was suddenly blown down by a hurricane. All three members of the family were buried in the rubble. By the time they were dragged out, they had all suffocated to death.

Hefei 100

Joint Suppression of Bandits at the Border of He Liu Counties: Bandits are rampant at the border of He Liu Counties. Some days ago, two gangs of bandits, Quan Chengchui and Zhang Wenzhong, robbed and kidnapped people in the Yulin Gang area. The Shuanghe Bandit Disaster Relief Committee, upon hearing the news, sent Captain Yang to lead a team to join the Shijiaqiao Defense Army in Liuan County, the Shangxia Bao Joint Village Association, and 500 members of the Red Spear Society to suppress them. They fought the bandits at Huang Dacang until night, when the bandits were finally unable to hold out and retreated towards Shu County. At that time, eight bandits were killed, and the two bandit leaders, Fang Qingxu and Wei Dasan, were captured alive, along with more than 20 bandits, all of whom were executed on the spot on the west bank. A total of 43 bandits were killed and 22 hostages were rescued. Liu Minzhi, the chief of the area, reported to the He Liu counties for the record on the 15th.

Education News

Important News

Jiangsu Province's Budget for Education Expenses for the 19th Year (Part Two) 101

(II) Revised Standards for Expenses of Students Studying in Europe, America, and Japan

Due to the different selection and supplementation periods for government-funded and subsidized students studying in European, American, and Japanese countries in Jiangsu Province, the amount of funding varies. In addition, the study abroad laws give additional national currency to the students studying in France and Belgium. The Jiangsu Department of Education has repeatedly received requests from government-funded and subsidized students that the high cost of gold and the low value of silver are affecting their studies, and they have requested that measures be taken to remedy this. After separately investigating the funding methods of various provinces for sending students abroad and considering that the study abroad expenses exceeded the budget by tens of thousands due to the impact of the high cost of gold last year, it is now specifically revised. For these students, the payment of gold currency in the country where they are studying is changed. It is estimated that an additional 20,000 yuan will be needed. It was proposed to the Jiangsu Education Expense Committee to increase the budget for study abroad expenses. Starting from the autumn of the 19th year, it is stipulated that all students studying abroad will be paid in the gold currency of the country where they are studying, and the additional tuition and experimental fees will be cancelled. The revised payment amounts are listed on the left:

United Kingdom (Government-funded): 20 pounds sterling per month per student

(Subsidized): 9 pounds sterling per month per student

Germany (Government-funded): 4 official marks per month per student

(Subsidized): 160 marks per month per student

France (Government-funded): 1,600 francs per month per student

(Subsidized): 600 francs per month per student

Belgium (Government-funded): 1,500 francs per month per student

(Subsidized): 600 francs per month per student

United States (Government-funded): 100 US dollars per month per student

(Subsidized): 45 US dollars per month per student

Japan (Government-funded): 90 yen per month per student

(Subsidized): 50 yen per month per student

In the future, the selection and supplementation of government-funded and subsidized students in Europe, America, and Japan will be based on the above-fixed standard expenses. However, the following items must still be handled separately: 1. French subsidized students who have received subsidies from the Sino-French University will still be given 400 yuan of national currency per year according to the old plan. 2. Japanese students who are supplemented with the Boxer Indemnity funds and whose subsidies have been approved under the old plan will still be given 240 yen per year according to the old plan.

(III) Budget Standards for Jiangsu Provincial Middle and Primary Schools for the 19th Year 102

Article 1: In order to achieve an average distribution of the recurring expenses of provincial middle and primary schools, the Department hereby stipulates the following standards for compliance.

Article 2: The recurring expenses standards of provincial middle schools are divided into the following three items: A. Salaries and wages: refers to the salaries of principals and staff, and the food expenses of servants. B. Tuition fees: refers to the salaries of teachers. C. Public miscellaneous expenses: refers to expenses such as stationery, postage, telecommunications, and the purchase of consumable miscellaneous items.

Article 3: The salaries and wages of each school under item A of the preceding article shall be distributed according to the following amounts:

A school with four grades or less: 5,784 yuan per year

A school with five grades: 7,338 yuan per year

A school with six grades: 8,892 yuan per year

A school with seven grades: 10,050 yuan per year

A school with eight grades: 11,208 yuan per year

A school with nine grades: 12,366 yuan per year

A school with ten grades: 13,524 yuan per year

A school with eleven grades: 14,682 yuan per year

A school with twelve grades: 15,840 yuan per year

A school with thirteen grades: 16,733 yuan per year

A school with fourteen grades: 17,626 yuan per year

A school with fifteen grades: 18,519 yuan per year

A school with sixteen grades: 19,412 yuan per year

A school with seventeen grades: 20,205 yuan per year

A school with eighteen grades: 21,198 yuan per year

A school with nineteen grades: 22,191 yuan per year

A school with twenty grades: 22,984 yuan per year

A school with twenty grades or more: 23,880 yuan per year

(Note) Schools with two or more buildings may increase by 20% according to the above standards.

Article 4: The amount of tuition fees for each school under item B of Article 2 is stipulated in units of grade. A. Each grade of junior high school is calculated at 1.25 yuan per hour for 34 hours per week, for a total of 2,040 yuan per year. B. For senior high school, single-track, each grade is calculated at 1.75 yuan per hour for 42 hours per week, for a total of 3,528 yuan per year. C. For senior high school, double-track, each grade is calculated at 1.75 yuan per hour for 37 hours per week, for a total of 3,108 yuan per year. The above standards include all required and elective courses.

Article 5: The public miscellaneous expenses of each school under item C of Article 2 are stipulated as follows: A. 1,000 yuan per grade per year for junior high schools with six grades or less. B. 1,300 yuan per grade per year for junior high schools with more than six grades. C. 1,200 yuan per grade per year for senior high schools with six grades and more than six grades. Its distribution: Zi. Postage and telecommunications: 5%. Chou. Purchase: 20% (this item must not be listed short). Yin. Consumption: 35% (experimental material fees should be fully distributed). Mao. Miscellaneous expenses: 25% (the reserve fund should account for more than 2% of the total expenses and be listed under the miscellaneous expenses item). When the distribution of the above Zi, Chou, Yin, and Mao four items does not need to reach the above standards, the remaining funds should be allocated to purchase expenses as much as possible.

Article 6: The expenses of rural normal schools shall be increased by 10% according to the above-listed junior high school expenses standards, and the distribution ratio shall be the same.

Article 7: The budget standards for middle school experimental primary schools are divided into four stages: A. Grades 1 to 3 are calculated at 1,625 yuan per grade. B. Grades 4 to 6, in addition to grade 3 being calculated according to item A, the remaining grades are calculated at 1,560 yuan per grade. C. Grades 7 to 9, in addition to grade 3 being calculated according to item A and grade 3 being calculated according to item B, the remaining grades are charged at 1,500 yuan per grade. D. For more than nine grades, in addition to grade 3 being calculated according to item A, grade 3 being calculated according to item B, and grade 3 being calculated according to item C, the remaining grades are calculated at 1,440 yuan per grade.

Article 8: The expenses of rural normal school experimental primary schools are stipulated at 1,040 yuan per grade per year.

Article 9: Each school shall prepare a budget in accordance with the budget overview stipulated by the Department and based on the above-listed articles.

Article 10: The temporary fees for the 19th year and the middle and primary school project fees decided by the Education Expense Committee will be separately approved and distributed.

High School Normal School Curriculum Review Committee 103

The Ministry of Education's Primary and Secondary School Curriculum Standards Drafting Committee convened a High School Normal School Curriculum Standards Review Committee at 9:00 AM on the 15th. Attendees included Ma Keta, Zhu Jingnong, Zhao Naichuan, Sun Benwen, Xia Chengfeng, Wu Yinyin, Gu Shusen, Dai Yingguan, Zheng Hesheng, Zhu Baoqin, Qiu Jingni, and Xu Yizhi (Representatives Qiu and Xu from the Central Party Headquarters). Gu Shusen served as Chairman, and Wang Linggen as Secretary. The meeting proceeded as scheduled: (1) The Chairman delivered an opening speech; (2) Section Chief Dai Yingguan reported on the drafting process; (3) Personnel were assigned to review each course; (4) Compulsory subjects for rural normal schools were discussed. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 AM. A second meeting was held in the Ministry's conference room at 8:30 AM on the 16th. Attendees included Wu Yinyin, Zhu Jingnong, Gu Shusen, Xia Chengfeng, Hu Dingan, Zheng Zonghai, Dai Yingguan, Huang Shouzhong, Zhao Naichuan, Ma Keta, Qiu Jingni, Sun Benwen, and Zhang Baihua. Gu Shusen served as Chairman, and Wang Linggen as Secretary. After the usual formalities, (1) Review reports were examined. (A) Health Education: It was resolved, based on the review report and with reference to the opinions of Zheng Zonghai and Zhao Naichuan, to revise and pass the measure. (B) Chinese Language: It was resolved to discuss the matter further after the reviewers have revised, printed, and distributed the materials. (C) Mathematics: It was resolved to discuss the matter further after the reviewers have revised, printed, and distributed the materials. (D) Chemistry: It was resolved to change lectures to two hours per week, while keeping the experimental time unchanged, for a total of six credits. The first item in the objectives and the last item of the minimum requirements for graduation were deleted. The rest was passed according to the review report. (E) Sociology: It was resolved to pass the measure according to the review report. (F) Music: It was resolved to reduce the elective credits for the normal school course by two and increase the music credits by two, combining "Applied Music for Elementary School Teachers" to a total of seven credits. The curriculum standards for this subject will be revised, printed, and distributed by the reviewers for further discussion. (G) Educational Testing: It was resolved to have Zheng Zonghai and Zhao Naichuan revise the format. (H) Principles of Education: It was resolved to pass the measure according to the review report, with modifications to be made if necessary when reviewing Educational Overview. (I) Educational Overview: It was resolved to have Zheng Zonghai and Zhao Naichuan revise the material with reference to Principles of Education. (J) Gymnastics: It was resolved to generally pass the measure according to the review report, with the standing committee members adjusting the wording. The meeting adjourned at 10:30 AM.

The Ministry of Education's Primary and Secondary School Curriculum Standards Drafting Committee continued its third review meeting of the High School Normal School curriculum standards, beginning at 8:30 AM on the 17th. Attendees included Li Zuyin, Ma Keta, Zhu Jingnong, Zhao Naichuan, Zheng Heting, Dai Yingguan, Huang Shouzhong, Xiong Zhengli, Zheng Zonghai, Zhu Baoqin, Xia Chengfeng, Hu Shuyi, Wu Yinyin, Gu Shusen, Xiong Zhugao, Xue Tianhan, Bai Jingni, Xu Yiqiao, and others. Gu Shusen served as Chairman, and Wang Linggen as Secretary. After the usual formalities, the review report results were as follows: (A) Educational Overview: It was resolved to pass the measure according to the review report. (B) Research on Elementary School Teaching Materials: It was resolved to change objective item three to item two and to revise the wording to "Develop the knowledge and skills to search for and trial-compile practical teaching materials for elementary schools." Objective item two was changed to item three. (C) Elementary School Teaching Methods: It was resolved to ask the three reviewers to revise and submit the material to the committee for soliciting opinions from the original drafters. (D) Elementary School Administration: It was resolved to add one credit; the rest was passed according to the review report. (E) Chinese Language: It was resolved to ask each reviewer to carefully review and submit their opinions to the committee within one week. (F) World History: It was resolved to pass the measure according to the review report. (G) Physics: It was resolved to pass the main points of the report, with the full text to be revised, printed, and distributed to each reviewer for careful review and submission of their opinions to the committee within one week. (H) National History: It was resolved to pass the draft and additionally invite Wu Yinyin, Li Qingsong, and Hu Shuyi to draft curriculum standards for Chinese and foreign history centered on questions, with a timeframe of one week. (I) Biology: It was resolved to pass the measure according to the review report. (J) Mathematics: It was resolved to add one credit and include a review of applied arithmetic, to be taught in the fifth semester. The content of this review will be supplied by the proposer and added to the draft for printing and distribution. Each reviewer should carefully review and submit their opinions to the committee within one week. (K) Applied Handicrafts for Elementary School Teachers: It was resolved to pass the measure according to the review report. (L) Applied Drawing for Elementary School Teachers: It was resolved to pass the measure according to the review report. (M) Applied Music for Elementary School Teachers: It was resolved to ask the reviewers of this course and the reviewers of the music course to merge the draft with the music draft for review.

The 11th Annual Meeting of the China Vocational Education Society and the National Federation of Vocational Education Institutions will hold its opening ceremony this morning in the auditorium of the French Elementary School building on Rue du Consulat. The exhibition will be held on the 5th floor of the Society premises from the 20th to the 22nd, open for viewing from 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM daily. Group meetings will be held from 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM on the 21st. The second plenary meeting will be held at 9:00 AM on the 22nd. The conference shorthand recording has been assigned to five gentlemen from the Chinese Shorthand Society: Gu Junquan, Wang Jianhou, Yang Xunxian, Pu Huawei.

Execution Status of Previous Motions: The execution status of the previous resolutions of the National Federation of Vocational Education Institutions is as follows: First, Education Administration Category: 1. Request the Central Government and request the Provincial Education Bureaus to hold provincial education conferences; 2. Vocational education should be incorporated into the educational organization and administrative system; 3. Submit to the Ministry of Education a request for the swift implementation of the resolution of the Vocational Education Group of the 17th National Education Conference to first organize a Vocational Education Committee; 4. Request the Central Educational Administration Authority to issue a circular to all provinces to conduct a thorough survey each year of the number of primary and secondary school students who have or have not continued their education after graduation, and to find ways to provide appropriate vocational education for those who have not continued their education. Second, Vocational Education Funding Category: 5. Designate special funds to be allocated for vocational education; 6. Vocational schools should stipulate funding for practical training equipment; 7. Determine vocational education funding. (Execution Status) The above seven articles have all been recorded and submitted to the Ministry for approval for future reference. Third, Vocational Education Teacher Training Category: 8. Primary and normal schools should add vocational subjects, and secondary and higher vocational schools should add education subjects; 9. Cultivate vocational education teachers; 10. Agricultural schools should pay attention to cultivating and improving rural talent; 11. Request the National Government to follow the Premier's teachings and quickly plan for fishery ports and establish more aquatic personnel training institutions to strengthen the nation's foundation and benefit the people's livelihood (The above two cases have been submitted to the Ministry but have not been approved). Fourth, Vocational Curriculum Category: 12. Vocational school students should be required to spend time on off-campus internships; 13. Vocational school courses should reduce theory, increase practical training, and use adaptation to social needs as the standard for establishing departments (The above two cases have been communicated to the Provincial Education Bureaus and vocational schools). 14. Vocational education in each province and county should pay attention to the mechanical industry (This case was cancelled). Fifth, Women's Vocational Education Category: 15. The standards for establishing departments in women's vocational schools should be adapted to women's special abilities, social trends, and local needs. Sixth, Worker Supplementary Education Category: 16. Request the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to strictly enforce worker supplementary education in accordance with factory regulations. Seventh, Vocational Guidance Category: 17. Request the Ministry of Education and separately communicate to the Provincial Education Bureaus to actively promote vocational guidance movements (The above four cases have been separately submitted to the Ministry). 18. Each secondary school and vocational school should establish a vocational guidance department or introduction department; 19. Regarding the employment prospects of vocational school graduates, request the Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mines to abolish the recruitment of non-agricultural school graduates as agricultural investigators (Recorded and replied to the Department of Agriculture and Mines); 20. Establish overseas vocational introduction offices and pay attention to colonization projects (Already implemented). All of the above resolutions have been organized and implemented by the China Vocational Education Society.

Municipal Education Bureau School Equipment Exhibition to Open 106

The Municipal Education Bureau will hold a school equipment exhibition on the 24th of this month. Eight rules of procedure have been drafted, which are recorded below: 1. The Standing Committee will designate display locations for each department; 2. The Standing Committee will distribute the registration forms submitted by each school to each director and, according to the number of school equipment items on each school's registration form, will distribute the first type of label to each school; 3. The director of each department will distribute the display locations according to the quantity of items and classification, and will compile a sub-number list of school equipment for each department and school; 4. When each school's equipment is sent to the Association for display, the director of each department will, together with the staff of the school in question, verify the numbered registration in accordance with the registration form

and affix the second type of label to the school equipment by the staff of the exhibiting school in accordance with the school equipment sub-number list, and a receipt will be issued; 5. After the school equipment is numbered, each department will classify and display it together with the staff of the exhibiting school; 6. Each department is responsible for safekeeping after the school equipment is displayed; 7. During the display period, visitors should be received by each department, and detailed explanations should be given if there are any inquiries; 8. When the school equipment is retrieved, each department will check the registration book and return it.

Chinese Expedition Football Team Arrives in Singapore (Zuodu) 112

South China Football Team Just Finished Competing in Singapore

The Expedition Team Arrives One After Another, Reducing the Warm Welcome

(Special Dispatch from Singapore, July 10th) The Chinese Expedition Football Team arrived in Singapore on July 1st via the Kanymaru Maru from Shanghai via Hong Kong. It was originally scheduled to arrive in Singapore at 5:00 PM yesterday (9th), but the ship failed to arrive on time, so it only berthed at Pier 18 at 6:30 AM this morning (10th). The enthusiasm for this trip to Singapore does not seem high. The number of people welcoming the team was not very large. Even the number of reporters from newspapers was less than thirty when the team arrived. Mr. Yu Zhuohua, President of the Chinese Sports Association, only arrived to welcome the team twenty minutes after the ship arrived. In short, the arrival of this team in Singapore was not as lively as the arrival of the Lok Wah team last time. However, when the Hong Kong South China team came to Singapore at the end of last month (6th), before the ship arrived, welcomers had already gathered with banners welcoming the South China team, waving in the wind. Furthermore, the ticket prices for domestic football teams coming to Singapore for competitions are extremely high. Taking the South China team's two matches in Singapore as an example, the second time, the ticket sales were only four-fifths of the first time. And since the competition between South China and the local Malaysian Chinese mixed team and the Singapore mixed team is not over ten days, the ticket issue for the upcoming expedition team is really worrying. When examining the passports, Yu Zhuohua said to Li Huitang, "I am afraid that people in Singapore will not enthusiastically welcome your team, because the South China team arrived not long ago (Now it is in the Malaysia Cup A competition)." After the passports were examined, passengers and other people went ashore at will, and many team members also landed. Li Huitang and Yu Hengzhi were still on board with Yu Zhuohua, discussing remedial measures for about twenty minutes before disembarking. By the time the photo was finished, it was already past 8:00 AM. How things will proceed, I will continue to report.

Japan Prepares for Sports Exhibition 116

(Special Correspondent) The Sports Council organized by the Japanese Ministry of Education has repeatedly consulted and sought rational promotion strategies for sports, and on July 8, the final consultation revised the resolution to answer the proposal on the control of sports organizations. A special committee will create a specific plan for implementation, and the requested budget for implementation expenses will be submitted for approval. Japanese authorities, in view of the extraordinary progress of sports, believe that the significance and effectiveness of sports have not yet been fully understood by the people, so they are eager to promote and popularize correct sports ideology. The Ministry of Education's Sports Division regards this as an urgent task at present and has carefully considered the following strategies: (1) Organizing sports exhibitions; (2) Regularly holding sports lectures; (3) Printing and distributing brochures to publicize the significance and effectiveness of sports as three key matters. Regarding the preparations for the exhibition, it is currently planned to start notifying local officials and powerful related organizations to collect display materials. With the goal of building a strong and healthy culture, the origin of sports to today's development will be covered. Local News

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Expresses Opinion on Foreign Intrusion of Police Power in Western Shanghai 119

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce is very indignant about the foreign intrusion into the police power in the Caojiadu area of western Shanghai by building roads beyond the boundary. At the executive committee meeting the day before yesterday, it was decided to take five measures to deal with it. This has been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. In addition to issuing a declaration, the Chamber of Commerce specially petitioned the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Municipal Government to follow the Prime Minister's instructions and promptly recover the concessions, and first recover the roads built beyond the boundary. At the same time, it also sent a letter to the Chinese taxpayers' association in the concessions, urging them to fight together. The original text is recorded as follows:

Petition to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: Regarding the foreign intrusion of police power in western Shanghai, it is urgent to negotiate and recover the roads built beyond the boundary by the Public Concession's Bureau of Public Works as soon as possible in order to fundamentally resolve the issue. I respectfully submit my humble opinion, hoping for your review and implementation. It has been found that the heads of the Jing'an Temple and Putuo Road police stations of the Public Concession in this city went to the Sixth District Police Station three days ago and requested that the police posts at Nos. 6, 7, 8, and 9 of Connaught Road, Singapore Road, and Edinburgh Road assigned by the district be revoked and replaced by police officers from the police station. A deadline of three days was given for a response. As of the 15th, the deadline had expired. The police station, because it did not receive a written reply from the acting director, sent an armed foreign police officer, leading six or seven Indian police officers, to patrol back and forth in the small vegetable market at the five corners of Edinburgh Road on the morning of the same day as a show of force. The Public Security Bureau, upon receiving the report, also dispatched a security team to the area to station. At more than 5:00 PM, the Jing'an Temple police station again sent two foreign police officers, eight Indian police officers, and more than ten Chinese police officers to the area to demonstrate. The Sixth District Police Station also sent more than 20 armed police officers to the area to guard it strictly. On the 16th, the Bureau of Public Works still simply sent a small number of patrol officers to patrol back and forth. The seventh and eighth police posts assigned by the Sixth District remained stationed in their original places. Acting Director Ren also dispatched a small number of security teams to patrol back and forth in the afternoon, but there was no confrontation like that on the 15th. When this situation was brought up for discussion at the second executive committee meeting of the affiliated association, it was generally believed that Edinburgh Road and other places were roads built beyond the boundary by the Bureau of Public Works, and all actions taken by foreigners in that area were infringements upon sovereignty, which our country has never recognized. Even in terms of police power, our country has gradually established police posts on the above-mentioned roads since the tenth year of the Republic of China. The police station has been indifferent to this. Now, it suddenly demands the withdrawal of police posts, and if its demands are not met, it intends to coerce with arms. Some commentators say that a third party is instigating this, and although the matter is confidential and difficult to speculate on, the cause of the conflict is all due to the construction of roads beyond the boundary. This matter has been negotiated for recovery many times, but after several years, there has been no result. If this case is not resolved for a day, our country's exercise of municipal power in that area will not be complete for a day, and there is a risk of side issues arising at any time. Now, your department is adhering to the Prime Minister's instructions and the central government's policies, and is still continuing to work hard to recover the treaty-established concessions. How can there be any hesitation in recovering the roads originally occupied and built beyond the boundary by foreigners, so as to prevent this from becoming a malignant tumor of municipal administration in this city and leaving behind a source of international provocation? All the reasons for preventing foreigners from seizing police power should start with recovering the roads built beyond the boundary, so as to achieve a fundamental solution. Therefore, I am writing to your department, hoping for your review, adoption, and implementation for the public good. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs (the petition to the Municipal Government is roughly the same, omitted).

Solemn Declaration: Since the Qing Dynasty, the opening of concessions has been stipulated in the treaties, specifying the four boundaries. The first article of the regulations of the concession north of the Yangjingbang River also first specifies the boundaries of the concession. Therefore, the so-called permission in Article 7 of the regulations to purchase land adjoining or separated from the concession for use as streets contradicts the provisions of Article 1 on boundaries. All land outside the concession is land under the jurisdiction of our country. How can the Bureau be allowed to arbitrarily dispose of land in our country that has not been opened based on the approval of the taxpayers' meeting (this is the original text of Article 7 of the regulations, referred to as "occupational landlords")? Therefore, Article 7 of the regulations, which is regarded by foreigners as the basis for building roads beyond the boundary, is, in strict legal terms, an act of encroachment. Our country's inherent sovereignty over that land cannot be infringed upon in the slightest. Moreover, in terms of facts, the Public Security Bureau has long established police posts and sent police officers to patrol Singapore Road, Edinburgh Road, and other places occupied and built beyond the boundary by foreigners since the 14th year of the Republic of China. The police station has long been at peace with this. Therefore, the so-called agreement between the "leader" and Sun Chuanfang has long been abandoned by the other party. How can it be used as a basis at this time? Therefore, the association believes that the police station's dispatch of a large number of armed patrol officers to the corner of Connaught Road and Edinburgh Road on July 15 to coerce the withdrawal of the police officers stationed there is tantamount to destroying the Bureau of Public Work's recent policies of seeking harmony with the Chinese people and improving Sino-foreign relations, which is deeply regrettable. Therefore, at the second executive committee meeting of the association on the 18th of this month, it was decided to issue the above declaration, hoping that the people residing in western Shanghai will unite to correct this erroneous action of the concession authorities, and hoping that the people of the country and the citizens of the city will make unremitting efforts and enthusiastic expressions in support of police power and the recovery of concessions.

Letter to the Taxpayers' Association: Dear Sirs, the Public Concession Patrol Station's request to the Sixth District Police Station of the Public Security Bureau to withdraw the police officers at Police Posts 7 and 8 at the corner of Connaught Road and Edinburgh Road on the 16th and 17th of this month, and the dispatch of a large number of armed patrol officers to coerce and cause disturbances because the request was not granted, must have been read in the newspapers long ago. The association held its second executive committee meeting yesterday. Because your association is a group of Chinese taxpayers, it has always made responsible expressions on major issues such as recovering national rights and protecting the interests of citizens, which are enough to attract the attention of foreigners residing in Shanghai. This time, the foreign intrusion of police power in western Shanghai in our country is tantamount to overturning the precedent of stationing police officers since the 14th year of the Republic of China, and is an attempt to uphold its extra rights on the roads occupied and built beyond the boundary, and is a further expression of opposition to the recovery of concessions. Judging from its nature, it is extremely serious. Why has your association not made any expression? Moreover, according to the regulations of your association, an executive committee meeting should be held every month. In recent months, no meeting has been convened, which is incomprehensible. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce is one of your members, and it is difficult to remain silent. It was decided that your association should immediately convene an executive committee meeting to fight together. I am sending this letter to inform you, hoping that you will investigate and handle it accordingly. Sincerely yours, Shanghai Chinese Taxpayers' Association.

Opportunity for India to Promote Chinese Silk 120

Confidential Report from Lu Chunfang, Consul General in India

Since Gandhi was arrested and imprisoned by the British government, the Indian people's resistance to British goods has become increasingly fierce. They welcome goods imported from other countries, especially silk. Lu Chunfang, our country's consul general in India, in view of this, secretly submitted a report to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting that it be forwarded to the Ministry of Commerce to order the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to send letters to various related organizations, dispatching personnel to India for on-site investigation and devising methods for improvement in order to develop trade with India. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has already sent letters to various silk industry organizations for investigation. The confidential report from Consul General Lu and the original letter from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce are recorded as follows:

Confidential Report from Consul General Lu: Regarding the confidential report that the Indian people are resisting British goods and that our country lacks banks and lawyers and cannot develop commerce and protect overseas Chinese, I respectfully submit my humble opinions for your review. I believe that the country's wealth comes from industry and commerce, and the people's security comes from the law. In recent years, the great powers have been paying attention to and promoting and protecting their respective countries' industries, commerce, and people at any time and any place. Our country's commerce has recently developed abroad, and there are nearly 10,000 overseas Chinese in India, all of whom are laborers. There are very few who are engaged in commerce, which is a major shortcoming. Since Gandhi was arrested by the British, the Indian people's resistance to British goods has become increasingly fierce. Even for daily necessities, all British products are rejected. They welcome goods imported from other countries. The opportunity for us to work together is once in a lifetime. There are three things that our country urgently needs to take advantage of. The first is to improve products. India's main products are tea and hemp, and the production of cloth is very small and of poor quality. The production of silk is even smaller. I saw that the shops in the New Market in that port were full of silk, with all kinds of colors, all produced by Japan, the United States, Britain, France, and other countries. I hardly saw any Chinese silk. When I asked the merchants of K.HSSARACO, they showed me two pieces of Chinese Huasi Ge and yellow silk. They said that the color was not durable and the quality was not strong. It would be damaged in one year, which was not as good as French silk, which could be used for three years. The silk from Japan and other countries is brightly colored and does not fade. Recently, the locals do not like to use Chinese silk. For this reason, there have been cases where customers bought silk in the store and returned it because it faded, so merchants do not sell Chinese silk. This situation is because our country's silk weaving factories and merchants lack research knowledge, which leads to commercial failure. Since India does not produce much silk and the Indian people do not use British goods, they cannot help but welcome the products of other countries. Our country is famous for its silk. If we can find a way to improve exports, we can recover our rights and interests. It is recommended that your department secretly consult the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, which will inform the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the Silk Industry Association, or factories, as well as the Cloth Industry Association, to dispatch experts to India for on-site investigation and improvement methods in order to develop industry and commerce and benefit foreign trade. This is in the public interest. Respectfully submitted to Minister of Foreign Affairs Wang.

Public Letter from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce: Dear Sirs, on the 18th of this month, we received an instruction from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, stating that a confidential report from the Consulate General in Calcutta had been approved and forwarded by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The proposed points were quite insightful. It is now a good opportunity for our country to develop foreign trade because the Indians are resisting British goods. In addition to sending separate letters of forwarding and reply, we are sending a copy of the original attachment for your information and for the information of the silk and cloth industries. Enclosed is a copy of the attachment. India's population is around 300 million, which is a very large market for sales. After the implementation of the boycott of British goods, it is an even better opportunity for the promotion of Chinese goods. However, it is necessary to conduct on-site investigations to determine which silk and cloth products suit Indian tastes in order to cater to current fashion. In accordance with the instructions, we are copying the original document and sending it to your association, requesting that you convene your colleagues to discuss it. If you can dispatch specialists to investigate and bring samples of durable quality to contact them, the manufacturers will have a better grasp of how to imitate them in the future. Since there is a Chinese consulate in that area, the consulate can be entrusted with handling the contact and guidance after arriving in India. Sincerely yours, (Xin Shanghai News Agency).

Both Northern and Southern City Rice Merchants Provide Guarantees 121

Social Affairs Bureau Approves Restoration to Original State

The number of Songjiang cargo ships arriving in the southern city with rice is not large, and they must be unloaded as soon as they arrive. Recently, because the Social Affairs Bureau registered and evaluated the rice, the rice merchants' associations agreed that this method of the Social Affairs Bureau was only to eliminate premium prices. If they could resolve to abide by the price limit and no longer disrupt it, there would be no need for evaluation. Each merchant provided a guarantee on the spot that they would not disrupt the price limit, and if they violated it, they would be willing to accept a fine of more than 1,000 yuan to be used for subsidized rice expenses. Zhu Zixiang was publicly elected to submit the report to the Social Affairs Bureau, and the bureau approved it yesterday, exempting them from evaluation and unloading. However, they should still follow the registration, and the chairman of the association, Zhu Zixiang, should be responsible for investigating and not showing favoritism or covering up. If there is any disruption and it is not reported, once the Social Affairs Bureau finds out, the penalty will be doubled. It is said that Zhu has informed the merchants, and the rice from the Northern and Changbang gangs will still be handled as before.

The rice merchants in the northern city convened a meeting of their colleagues the day before yesterday, chaired by Jiang Zisheng, who explained the difficulties. Only if the colleagues no longer disrupted the price limit could it be lifted. After a long discussion, they dispersed late at night. It is said that they decided to follow the method of the cargo ship rice merchants' association, with each merchant providing a guarantee with a seal that they would no longer disrupt the price limit of 21 yuan, and if they violated it, they would be willing to accept a fine of 1,000 yuan. Jiang Zisheng and Fu Qiangeng were publicly elected to submit the report to the Social Affairs Bureau. Last night, the North City Office received a reply, which roughly stated, "The rice industry in the northern city has disregarded orders and disrupted the price limit, and has repeatedly failed to correct its behavior despite warnings. For the sake of the food for the entire city, the bureau has no choice but to take decisive measures. Now that the rice merchants have been able to repent of their past mistakes and strictly abide by the orders, and have obtained guarantees that they will no longer disrupt the price limit, and are willing to accept a fine of 1,000 yuan for any secret premium prices, they are provisionally allowed to register the incoming rice ships with the registration office of the bureau from the 20th of this month, and the merchants will sign samples for evaluation and sale. The association must still be responsible for investigating and the merchants must supervise each other, and must not condone or cover up. If there are any acts of disrupting the price limit and they are not reported, in addition to doubling the amount of the fine according to the guarantee, the association and the merchants who jointly signed the guarantee will be held accountable. Please inform everyone to abide by this."

Provincial Committee to Inspect the Sea Dike in Baoshan 122

The Baoshan Sea Dike was damaged for hundreds of zhang after being hit by a hurricane and storm surge, and it is about to collapse. Wang Yizhong, director of the Jiangnan Dike Engineering Office, telegraphed the provincial government, requesting that funds be allocated quickly for emergency repairs. This was recorded in the previous report. It is now learned that Director Wang received a reply telegram from the Provincial Construction Department yesterday, stating that Pei Zhenrong had been appointed to Baoshan to inspect the dangerous situation of the project on the ground so that he could consult the Finance Department and allocate funds for emergency repairs. According to the authorities of the office, the Baoshan Sea Dike was built in the eleventh year of the Qing Dynasty Yongzheng period. At that time, Hu Renji, the county magistrate of the county, used his private family property to build it. Later generations were grateful for his virtue and erected a shrine to commemorate him. However, for hundreds of years since then, it has never been thoroughly repaired and is in a dilapidated state. If it collapses once, the surrounding counties may become a swamp. The danger can be imagined. The total length of the sea dike is more than 1,300 zhang, from Wusong Paotai Bay to Lion Grove. The most recent damage is in the area north of Wuyue Dunshi, about 400 zhang, which requires 140,000 yuan. If the entire dike is to be repaired, it will require more than 2 million yuan.

Money Industry Association Decides on Two Important Cases 123

Plan to Seek Safety Due to Lack of Silver Dollars

Plan to Prepare Early for Year-End Closing

The North City Money Industry Association proposed two important cases to regulate finance and seek safety. They were decided at a meeting the day before yesterday. The full text of the proposals and the details of the decisions are recorded below. (1) Shanghai is a major port for international trade. All transactions with foreign merchants, including the prices of goods entering and leaving, are settled in taels first. In the past, the price of taels fluctuated according to the price of large bars, but now it is the opposite. This is because the import and export of various goods cannot offset each other, resulting in this phenomenon. In Shanghai, silver dollars are circulated in addition to standard silver, and the Shanghai Mint is actively proceeding with silver dollar minting. The raw materials depend on large bars. It is found that the import of large bars has been very small recently. According to the newspapers, the number of commonly used silver dollars shipped to other ports is also not small. Judging from the current situation, the silver dollars circulating in the market are not very abundant. There are two reasons for this: (a) because of the needs of various ports, shipments continue; (b) because various banks store more cash in preparation. It is conceivable that silver dollars circulating in the market are not very abundant because of these two reasons. What is even more worrying is that large bars do not come, and silver dollars are decreasing day by day. If the export of goods remains sluggish, foreign merchants and banks will inevitably ship precious silver to foreign countries to offset the taels owed. Even if the Shanghai Mint can start smelting and casting immediately, there is a risk of a lack of raw materials. The autumn harvest has not yet begun, and the demand for silver dollars is not very urgent, but the price of foreign currency has already risen so much, and the situation is so dangerous. The anxieties are extreme. Our colleagues in the financial industry are the first to bear the brunt if there is a risk in the financial industry. We should discuss how to seek safety in advance. This is the first case. (2) Change to the National Calendar. Our colleagues have long followed the business community in closing accounts at the end of each year, except for pre-ordered long-term accounts. All receivables and payables must be cleared at this time so that the final settlement can be performed to determine the profit and loss of the year. At the end of last year, because of the change to the National Calendar, preparations were not completed in time, and the government approved a one-month extension. Now that the National Calendar has been changed, the year-end closing will naturally be handled at the end of the National Calendar year, without any doubt. However, many merchants in the interior still use the abolished calendar. Shanghai is a commercial hub, and the money industry has the responsibility of financial circulation. Usually, whether cash or goods are released to various industries, they must be passed from A to B to C, and so on. By the end of the year, C pays to B, and B returns to A, and the final result is in the financial industry. If the year-end closing of the National Calendar this year cannot be completed on schedule due to the habits of various places, our colleagues will face a great danger. We should discuss how to seek safety in advance. This is the second case. After much discussion on the above two cases, in order to reduce the risk for our colleagues, the only way is to reduce the amount of loans at any time. However, reducing the amount of loans will inevitably affect various industries, which is not a good policy. After careful consideration, the first case should request the government to make overall plans as soon as possible to ensure that the supply and demand of silver dollar raw materials are equal, so that there will be no fear of financial panic and the market can be stable. For the second case, although the year-end closing of the National Calendar is still far away, we must plan ahead. It is natural to close accounts at the end of the National Calendar year. Our colleagues should publish notices in newspapers in advance and send letters to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce and the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to notify the national business community to uniformly use the National Calendar, so that there will be no excuses at the year-end closing of the National Calendar. This is the most complete plan for the National Calendar to be implemented in the commercial community without facing dangerous situations.

French Concession Tram Ticket Seller Severely Beaten Yesterday 125

Company Decides to Suspend All Services Today

At 6:15 yesterday morning, Tram No. 111 on French Route 2, which runs from Xujiahui to the Sixteen Pups, was just starting from the Lujiabang Depot when it arrived at the intersection of Route Lafayette and Route Luban. Dozens of people resembling workers were ambushed there in advance, each with iron bars and stones hidden on their bodies. At a signal, they rushed forward, first throwing stones at the tram, and then dragging the driver and three ticket sellers out of the tram and beating them with bars. The detectives who were guarding the tram nearby rushed to the scene and arrested four people on the spot. The three beaten men were seriously injured and groaned on the ground. It is estimated that the waist of ticket seller No. 179 was the most severely injured, and his life was in danger. Ticket seller No. 114 was injured in the head, but it was not a problem. The driver of Tram No. 169 was only slightly injured. The detectives first sent the injured to Guangci Hospital and then escorted the four arrested people to the police station to be detained separately for questioning by the French Concession Public Court. It is said that only six trams were dispatched from the depot yesterday morning, and Tram No. 111 was the second to be dispatched. By 5:40 in the evening, all services had been completely suspended. It is said that the company authorities have decided to suspend all services today.

Various Circles Establish Standing Committee for Fundraising 126

And Designate Four Banks as Donation Collection Points

The Shanghai All-Circles Fundraising Association for Relieving War-Affected Civilians and慰劳Frontline Soldiers held its first joint meeting of various groups at 3:00 PM yesterday. More than 20 people, including Yu Qingqia, Yu Hongjun, Zhu Yingpeng, Qian Xinzhi, Ye Huijun, Wang Yiting, Wang Binyan, Zhao Tieqiao, Zheng Yuxiu, and Zheng Huichen, attended the meeting. After discussion, it was decided to change the name of the preparatory committee to the Fundraising Association, and Yu Qiaqing, Chen Dezheng, Hu Mengjia, Ye Huijun, and Sanyi Ting were elected as standing committee members. The Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Central Bank of China, and the Shanghai City Bank were designated as donation collection points. The office location will be at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Establishment of the National Coal Production and Sales Association 127

Election of Executive Committee and Supervisory Committee Members

The inaugural meeting of the National Coal Production and Sales Association of the Republic of China was held yesterday at 2:00 PM at the National Federation of Commerce venue. Representatives from the Municipal Government, including Zhu Wei Yao, Lin Kang Hou from the National Federation of Commerce, Jin Sheng Bai from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, along with Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Xinfu, Yu Shunqing, Wang Jie'an (represented by Xu Genghua), Wu Keqiang, Chuan Ruiquan, Xu Kesheng, Chen Zhiying, and over a hundred coal merchant representatives, attended the meeting. After the meeting commenced, Lin Kang Hou was publicly elected as chairman, Feng Huimin as master of ceremonies, and Lin Shanqiu as recorder. Following the ceremonial procedures, the chairman delivered an opening address, stating, in essence, that the establishment of the National Coal Production and Sales Association marks the beginning of a revitalized coal industry. In recent years, domestic industries have suffered due to the impact of war. Although there are genuine domestic goods, transportation has been hindered, preventing their distribution. Our country is rich in coal resources, but due to the aforementioned reasons, we can only passively watch foreign coal dominate the market. We can only hope that the war ends soon, allowing all industries to gradually recover. When transportation is no longer obstructed, domestic coal can be transported both domestically and internationally, and patriotic citizens can purchase and use it as much as possible. Following this, Mr. Yu Shunqing, who had been preparing for the association for over a year, rose to speak, saying, "The more civilized the world becomes, the more intense the competition for survival becomes. This is a principle of natural selection that has been consistent throughout history. The key to survival is economics, which is crucial to the security of a nation and the success or failure of an individual. Therefore, there are economic scholars in ancient times and economic departments today, dedicated to studying and debating economics. How important is the application of economics! Since the opening of our country to foreign trade, customs have become increasingly extravagant, and habits have become indulgent, leading to the market being dominated by foreigners. The outflow of money is unknown to be in the tens of millions. However, our people are unaware and willingly become the prey, resulting in the impoverishment of the people and the exhaustion of wealth. If this continues, the country will cease to exist. As citizens, we have a responsibility for the prosperity of our nation and are concerned day and night. Therefore, starting in 1923, I engaged in the investigation of a portion of coal-related matters. The investigation revealed that our country loses as much as 200 million yuan annually in the coal industry. As a result, I vowed to write and promote my views on domestic coal, hoping to awaken the people. However, my individual efforts are insufficient, and success cannot be achieved without collective effort. Therefore, I gathered like-minded individuals to establish this association. I am grateful to Mr. Lin Kang Hou of the National Federation of Commerce for his support and for sending telegrams on behalf of the association to various departments of the National Government, provincial governments, and chambers of commerce. The National Government also issued an order to promote the association. Therefore, the reputation of this association should be attributed to Mr. Lin. This is the history of my involvement in the establishment and preparation of this association."

Following this, representatives from the Municipal Government and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce delivered speeches. Subsequently, executive and supervisory committee members were elected. The executive committee members are Lin Kang Hou, Yu Shunqing, Xu Wusun, Liu Yumen, Zhang Xinfu, Wu Keqiang, Zhou Yan, Zhang Zujie, Xu Kesheng, Yuan Ludeng, Zhao Tieqiao, Fang Jiaobo, Chen Bogang, Wang Xiaolai, and Sheng Pihua, with alternates Xie Luxi, Chen Ganqing, Shao Zhizhan, Lin Qinxiang, and Chen Shuntong. The supervisory committee members are Yu Qiaqing, Yuan Duanfu, Tu Diaoyun, Chen Zhiying, Zhao Jinqing, Li Zushen, and Gu Xinyi, with alternates Su Biting, Shen Zhongyi, and Jiang Chunchun. The meeting adjourned after a photograph was taken.
