Both Railways Still Selling Tianjin-Pukou Joint Tickets 130

Sales Have Not Actually Been Suspended

Regarding the news reported yesterday that the two railways had temporarily suspended the sale of Tianjin-Pukou Railway joint passenger tickets, we received letters yesterday from Mr. Liu Chengchang, Director of the Traffic Department, and Mr. Zheng Baozhao, Deputy Director, stating that the joint ticket sales for the two railways were approved by the Railway Department's Joint Transportation Office on the 18th of this month. Due to the insufficient number of passenger cars on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, the sale of joint tickets was temporarily suspended. However, on the afternoon of the same day, another telegram was received from the Joint Transportation Office stating that Tianjin-Pukou joint transportation would resume to Yanzhou from that day onward. The Traffic Department immediately telegraphed all related stations to comply. Therefore, in fact, joint transportation has not been suspended, and this correction is being made.

The Ministry of Finance's Order Urging the Financial Bureau to Remit Funds is Inaccurate 131

Regarding the news reported on the 18th about the Ministry of Finance ordering the Municipal Finance Bureau to remit funds, a key official from the Finance Bureau stated that the bureau's monthly income consists of local tax revenues and does not include national tax funds. Therefore, the funds are used locally according to the budget. Not only has the bureau never remitted funds to the Ministry of Finance, but the Ministry of Finance has also never ordered the bureau to remit funds. This news is not only untrue but also erroneous and is likely motivated by other purposes.

Wages for Holidays Commemorating the Revolution 132

Should Be Paid in Accordance with the Law

The Municipal Government Issues a Notice to All Businesses

The Municipal Government, due to the fact that some Chinese-owned yarn factories in the city have not been paying their workers for holidays commemorating the revolution, which violates national laws, has presented a request to the Social Affairs Bureau to issue a notice to all Chinese and foreign-owned businesses to comply with the payment of wages. The government issued a notice yesterday, stating: "Regarding the matter of the notification, the dates of official holidays for workers in the city have been approved by the Executive Yuan and announced. It has been found that the majority of businesses in the city pay their workers during the legally designated revolutionary holidays, but there are still many that do not. This situation is not equitable and violates national laws. Therefore, compliance should be uniform to avoid bias and prevent excuses. The Social Affairs Bureau has requested that a notice be issued, which is hereby approved. All businesses in the city are hereby notified to comply. It should be known that since the holidays commemorating the revolution have been stipulated, workers should be paid for their holidays, and no one should violate this, so as not to cause inconvenience. This notice is hereby issued."

Both Labor and Management Should Abide by the Law 133

Separate Orders Issued by the Social Affairs Bureau

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, based on the resolution of the previous representatives' assembly, submitted a request to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to instruct the labor force to jointly abide by the Law on the Handling of Labor Disputes. It also cited the incident of the Chamber of Commerce's donation collection personnel being assaulted on the road as a violation of human rights and requested a reaffirmation of government orders. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau immediately issued instructions, stating: "The request has been noted. Since the Law on the Handling of Labor Disputes was promulgated by the National Government and announced by this bureau in Notice No. 133, both labor and management must strictly comply. There is no need for further notification. However, in reality, both labor and management sometimes deliberately violate the law. This is because their prejudices against each other are too deep. Once a dispute arises, they become emotional and exceed the boundaries of normal behavior. In addition to issuing a general order to all labor unions in the city to sternly warn them, you must also instruct the employers of each industry to comply, eliminate prejudices, and abide by the law. Only then can labor and management understand each other and resolve disputes. As for the protection of human rights, the law is in place. If the alleged assault on the donation collection personnel of the Chamber of Commerce is true, a criminal lawsuit can be filed with the judicial authorities in accordance with the law. The request for reaffirmation is beyond the scope of this bureau's authority and will not be considered." This instruction was also issued to all labor unions, stating: "Regarding the matter of complying with orders, the law stipulates that people cannot be exempt from responsibility because they are unaware of the law. However, since the promulgation and implementation of the regulations related to the labor union's handling of labor disputes, both labor and management have often violated the regulations. Regardless of whether their actions are intentional or unintentional, they are still violations of the law. Supporting labor is one of the main policies of our party. We are reluctant to punish without teaching, but condoning and relaxing the law would not be fair. Therefore, you are hereby ordered to comply, constantly educate the workers, and be cautious not to test the law. Do not be negligent. This order is hereby issued."

Recent Statistics on Vaccination by the Health Bureau 134

More Than 260,000 People Have Benefited

This year, the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau's cholera prevention efforts have been expanded compared to previous years. The Propaganda Committee promotes and urges vaccinations, and the Vaccination Teams implement the vaccinations. This has awakened the public's belief in epidemic prevention. In previous years, the number of people vaccinated against cholera was around 150,000, but this year, from May 1st to July 15th, it has reached 266,361, and it is still being promoted. This vaccination work is a pioneering effort in our country. Even in countries with earlier public health development, it was not easy to achieve this result when first implementing vaccination. According to people in the bureau, if the concession areas could jointly implement widespread vaccination, the cholera epidemic that Shanghai dreads every year could be eliminated, and the number of citizens dying from cholera would be greatly reduced. However, due to various practical constraints, disease statistics have not yet been fully compiled. Therefore, the effectiveness of this prevention work is difficult to express in numbers. However, the principle of health administration is to eliminate problems before they arise. The bureau's only hope is that citizens will abandon their prejudices, accept vaccination, and make it as widespread as possible. It is hoped that people from all walks of life with higher awareness will assist and guide them to accept vaccination.

The Petition of the Western Paint Association 135

The Municipal Western Paint Industry Association, the Silk and Satin Dyeing Industry Association, the Qinglan Dyeing Industry Union, etc., submitted a document to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating that non-member businesses should jointly abide by the resolutions and approved rules of the industry association. The document stated that they jointly support the Municipal Market Industry Association's proposal that "the rules approved by the competent authorities for filing should be regarded as special regulations for the industry, and non-member businesses should also jointly abide by them." They requested that it be forwarded to the Legislative Yuan of the National Government and consulted with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for adoption and implementation to protect industry and commerce and benefit the people. The letter was respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce for review. It was stated that at the inaugural meeting of the Chamber of Commerce on the 21st of last month, the Municipal Market Industry Association, the Shoe Industry Association, the Flour Industry Association, and the preparatory committee of the Chinese and Foreign Department Store Association proposed the following: "(1) Merchants who have established an industry association, even if they have not joined the association, should abide by the resolutions of the association. If they violate the resolutions, the association may file a lawsuit in accordance with the law. (2) The rules submitted by various industry associations to the competent government authorities for approval should be regarded as regulations promulgated by the government and have a very precise legal status. Non-member businesses should also be subject to sanctions. (3) There are many violations of the approved rules. How to remedy this should be discussed." The Chamber of Commerce believes that the effectiveness of the resolutions of the industry association cannot extend to merchants who have not joined the association. However, the rules jointly formulated by each industry are originally intended to protect business and regulate operations. They must also be submitted to the competent government authorities for record filing. If there is a risk of bias or monopoly, they will not be approved by the government. After this approval process, their nature is different from the individual decisions of the association and similar to the regulations specially formulated by the government for each industry. It seems that both member and non-member businesses should be bound by them. Otherwise, members must fulfill various obligations and consider the public interest, and be subject to the restrictions of the rules. Non-members can freely expand their private interests. Inevitably, members will regret joining, and the group will disintegrate. It is also feared that cunning people will rely on having joined to control the industry on the one hand, and use capital to open stores and arbitrarily expand their private interests on the other hand. The consequences are unimaginable. This situation has been discovered repeatedly by the various industry associations in the city. The original proposal of the Municipal Market Industry Association is not without insight. Therefore, based on the above opinions, the proposal was combined and submitted to the Chamber of Commerce for resolution at the general meeting. It was stated that the above proposal is a clear and firm plan for the various industry associations in the city to resolve their troubles. With unanimous agreement, the associations jointly support the above proposal and jointly submit it to the Chamber of Commerce for review. It is requested that it be promptly forwarded to the Legislative Yuan of the National Government and consulted with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for adoption and implementation to protect industry and commerce and benefit the people. The letter was respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

A Record of the Grand Gathering Yesterday to Welcome Mei Lanfang 136

Ancient Music of the Datong Music Society Was Pleasing to the Ear

Mei Lanfang's Reply Was Very Humble

Yesterday was the second day after Mei Lanfang's return from the New World. Celebrities from the sea and leaders from various industries gathered at the Great China Hotel to welcome him. The guests and hosts sweated and conversed, which was also a pleasant event in the sweltering heat. Mr. Mei had been abroad for half a year and was highly acclaimed overseas. Although yesterday's welcome tea party was also a kind of social gathering, it was the first time Mr. Mei met with people from all walks of life after his long journey and return to his country. The general situation of the grand meeting is recorded as follows to inform the readers.

The venue for the return of the guest from the New World was set in the Italian Garden of the Great China Hotel, accompanied by the ancient music of the Datong Music Society. Guests who came to the place felt the wonder of the intermingling of Chinese and Western cultures. In addition to the 44 hosts mentioned in yesterday's newspaper, Chinese and Western guests were gathered together, and some brought their families with them. There was a mix of shoes and clothing, and the shadows of hair and the fragrance of clothing. Mr. Mei's popularity can be said to be complete. After the guests were assembled, Mr. Mei entered the venue and nodded to greet each of them. He was wearing a black gown and white shirt, and his demeanor was relaxed. He held a paper folding fan in his hand. He exchanged pleasantries with the guests briefly. The talk and manners of the returning guest from the New World in the minds of the people were still the same as before.

Li Shizeng's Speech Zheng Qinwen, the conductor of the Datong Music Society, led the members to play five chapters of national music. The sound of the zither, pipa, bells, and drums resonated, and the guests all tapped their feet and praised. After the music stopped, applause rang like thunder. Then, Chairman Li Shizeng stood up. The chairman of yesterday's welcome meeting was originally Mayor Zhang, but Zhang was unable to attend. Mr. Li began by explaining this. Next, he said that Mr. Mei's success on this trip was the success of Chinese drama, and it was also the realization of the intermingling of Chinese and Western cultures. However, he also elaborated that the elements of opera, including art education, are not trivial. Chinese drama, even without seeking publicity abroad, has its own considerable value. The same is true for Western drama. There is no need to go to extremes. One can learn from the strengths of others and make up for one's own shortcomings. Finally, he said that Mr. Mei's return on this trip will give a new life to Chinese opera. He hoped that Mr. Mei would work hard. His speech was translated into English by Mr. Xie Fusheng, and Mr. Yu Qiaqing also gave a speech on the spot, expressing his admiration for Mr. Mei.

Hu Shi's Speech Dr. Hu Shi spoke after Mr. Yu, saying that Mei Lanfang's success was the success of Mr. Mei himself. As for the issue of Chinese drama, it should be discussed separately. Dr. Hu further said that Mr. Mei's success was due to his personal cultivation. If it were someone else, it would not be certain whether they could return with this reputation. Finally, he said that before returning to China, Mei Lanfang wrote to friends in Shanghai, stating that he felt more and more ashamed as he was welcomed and praised everywhere. He asked, "What ability do I have to receive this excessive praise? In the future, I must study the path of drama more and put in more effort." The doctor said that just from this, it can be seen that Mr. Mei is humble and his success is not accidental. As for the mutual help of Mr. Mei's friends, it is not just for Mr. Mei alone. Ye Gongchuo was the last person to speak in the speech, and he added to Dr. Hu Shi's "Mr. Mei's personal success," saying that Mr. Mei's success in the United States need not be said. What is especially important is that Mr. Mei introduced Chinese drama to foreigners, allowing them to know the truth about Chinese drama and avoid vague guesses. Before Mr. Mei set out, his colleagues predicted that his success could be expected. Now it is indeed the case. It is also enough to see that Mr. Mei's artistic achievements have surpassed others.

Li Shizeng and Mei Lanfang at the Welcome Dinner

Mei Lanfang's Reply Amid the applause of the people, Mei Lanfang stood up to give his reply, speaking in extremely pure Mandarin, with each word clearly and distinctly, which the listeners could hear clearly. His words were as follows: "Lanfang is able to realize his dream of going to the United States thanks to the encouragement of the gentlemen and the advocacy of the Beijing Opera Academy. This trip has already been half a year. Lanfang's purpose in going to the United States was for my own learning, knowledge, and skills, because I have always lacked a foundation and lacked research. Therefore, I wanted to go out and see what other people have to offer, or perhaps I could gain some benefit. After arriving in New York, I originally wanted to go and study first, but all parties hoped that I could perform first. Therefore, I decided to perform for two weeks. As a result, I performed for five weeks. New York's reviews of our Chinese opera were very good. The newspapers often had records of our opera. They all praised the depth and mystery of our Chinese culture. Therefore, other places sent letters and people inviting me to perform. Some places, because of time and arrangement issues, were not convenient, so I only went to a few big places. From New York, I went to Chicago, where I performed for ten days, and then to San Francisco, where I performed for two weeks. Then I went to Los Angeles. Los Angeles is very close to Hollywood. I performed for ten days in Los Angeles. Then we went to Honolulu. The overseas Chinese there have a very strong interest in the motherland. Therefore, the results everywhere were very good. The above paragraph proves that this trip was really too busy because of the performances, and I can't say anything about the research aspect. If someone were to ask me about American drama, I'm afraid I would still have to ask others. As for the reputation I gained from performing, that is even less worth mentioning, because what I performed is only one genre, and I always feel that it is not up to the meaning of art. Now that I think back, before Lanfang set out, I received the strong support of all the gentlemen. After arriving in the United States, the Americans gave me very good reviews, and many overseas Chinese were also very enthusiastic. In Lanfang's view, this is not just a small personal honor, and even a small success in Chinese drama is a small matter. Perhaps there are still larger relationships involved. When Lanfang went out, I was often very apprehensive. Today, I am very ashamed that all the gentlemen have opened such a grand gathering. After returning this time, Lanfang feels even more that my knowledge is shallow, but I will never dare to fail the kindness and expectations of all the gentlemen. From now on, I will prepare to work hard and research drama. If there is an opportunity, I want to go out again to see the progress of others. Therefore, I have this determination to repay all the gentlemen and the overseas Chinese in the United States for their kindness to me."

240 Miles Across

Appears to be Heading Towards China

Chen Xiaoyu Was Kidnapped on Avenue Road Last Night 139

Chen Intended to Drive to See His Concubine

Unexpectedly Encountered Danger When Leaving Home

Gunshots Frightened Away an Old Woman

The Car Is Still Missing

At around 8:00 PM yesterday, Chen Xiaoyu, who lives at No. 1361, the corner of Avenue Road and Hart Road, was suddenly kidnapped by four bandits in front of his house. Chen's own car, No. 4702, was also driven away by the bandits and has disappeared. The details of the kidnapping are as follows:

Family Situation Chen Xiaoyu is 33 years old and from Fujian. His grandfather, Chen Quanru, once served as the Superintendent of the Tianjin Customs, and his family had a reputation in the officialdom. The Chen family has lived in Shanghai for many years. They currently reside at No. 1361 Avenue Road, living comfortably and not engaged in production. It is said that Chen once made a bet on gold transactions last year, resulting in a huge loss of assets.

Bandits Lay in Wait Chen has a six-cylinder Buick sedan, with rental concession license plate number 4702, driven by a driver, Lu Guisheng, from Suzhou. Chen has a concubine and built a golden house in the Yongning Village on Foch Road in the French Concession. At around 8:00 PM last night, Chen planned to drive there. He walked out of the house with his driver, Lu Guisheng. Unexpectedly, four bandits were lying in wait in front of the door.

Disguised as Vendors The four bandits disguised themselves as vendors selling melons, peanuts, and other snacks. They lingered in front of Chen's house for a long time. When they saw Chen and the others leaving the house and approaching the car, they swarmed forward. Two bandits kidnapped Chen into the car. One bandit was responsible for driving, and one bandit pushed the driver, Lu Guisheng, out of the car. At that time, the front of the car was facing north, and it drove all the way towards Jing'an Temple and disappeared. A Shot in the Air The house opposite Chen's is a broker shop. An old woman in the shop saw the four bandits wrestling with Chen and Lu. Thinking it was a normal fight, she hurried over to mediate. At this time, the bandits had already succeeded and pushed Lu Guisheng down. Seeing the old woman approaching breathlessly, thinking that she had malicious intentions, they quickly took out a pistol and fired a shot in the air. With a loud bang, the car had already started, and the old woman was also frightened away.

Interrogation of the Driver After being pushed down by the bandits, Lu Guisheng stood there for a while. Seeing that his master had been kidnapped, he returned home to report. Soon, the detectives arrived and took Lu to the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station for interrogation. The police are tracking the car that was robbed, but it has not yet been found.

Huang Yuyi Escapes Danger 140

Yesterday, He Took a Steamer to Southeast Asia for Recuperation

Huang Yuyi, the assistant manager of the Zhongnan Bank, was kidnapped by bandits on Haig Road at 6:30 PM on May 27th. For over a month, there was no news. Huang suddenly returned home safely at around 1:00 AM the day before yesterday (the 18th). It is reported that after Huang was kidnapped, he was hidden in a small house near Hongqiao Road in western Shanghai. At around 6:00 PM on the 17th, Huang took advantage of the guards relaxing in the cool air and escaped through the door. Two bandits saw him and immediately chased after him with guns. They were only about ten steps away. The bandits fired two shots at Huang. Huang fell to the ground in panic and did not dare to move. It was sunset, and there were many pedestrians in the fields. The bandits saw Huang fall to the ground and not move, so they stopped chasing him. After a short while, Huang saw that the bandits had disappeared, so he got up and fled for his life. After walking for about half an hour, he arrived near the back of Jiaotong University. Because there was a small stream in the way, he detoured to the front gate of the university, intending to borrow a telephone and hire a car to return home. However, Huang had just escaped from the bandits' den, his hair was long, his face was dirty, and he was still wearing a lined robe, looking very miserable, and he could not communicate, so he was prevented from entering by the gatekeeper of the university. Helpless, he hired a rickshaw to

Page 16

search for his own residence in the French Concession. Because he could not communicate and was not familiar with the roads, he wandered around various roads for more than four or five hours, changing rickshaws three times before finally arriving home. His family was overjoyed to see him. Huang stayed in the bandits' den for fifty-two days, but his spirit was still good. Yesterday, he took a steamer to Southeast Asia for a long period of recuperation.

Qiu Jianfei Escapes Danger 141

Planning an Escape from the Bandits' Den

Yesterday, He Went to Suzhou and Wuxi for Relaxation

Qiu Jianfei, a famous amateur actor, was kidnapped near the Grand Stage on Hankou Road at around 1:00 AM on the 5th of this month while returning home after watching a play. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. Half a month has passed, and now we learn that Qiu suddenly escaped from the bandits' den at 11:00 PM the night before last. Upon hearing the news, this newspaper's reporter went to Qiu's residence to inquire about the details. Mr. Zhang, a friend of Qiu, received him and said that after Qiu was kidnapped, the bandits directly hid him in a small boat in a canal. There were three or four bandits waiting in the boat. At that time, Qiu was too frightened and could not recognize the address, but he guessed that it was probably in the Riyue Bridge area in western Shanghai. After boarding the boat, he was locked in a narrow cabin. The temperature was very high and suffocating. The bandits all spoke with a northern accent, in groups of three to five, taking turns guarding with guns. Although Mr. Qiu repeatedly begged for a little ventilation, he had to wait until late at night and could only sit briefly at the bow of the boat before being asked to return to the cabin, as if he were a criminal in prison. At first, the bandits suspected that Qiu was a young master of the Qiu Tianbao Silver Shop. After the explanation was made clear, the bandits appeared quite frustrated. Until the night before last, Qiu repeatedly asked the bandits to let him lie on the deck, saying that if they were not at ease, they could tie his hand to the guard's hand and sleep together. The bandits listened to him, smiled, and agreed. At that time, he slept with two bandits on the bow of the boat. At around 11:00 PM, both bandits were fast asleep, snoring loudly. Although Qiu had the intention to escape at that time, he was afraid that the bandits were pretending, and he saw that the boat was about seven or eight feet away from the shore. So he deliberately tossed and turned frequently. Seeing that the two bandits were snoring as usual, Mr. Qiu then firmly grasped the cable with one hand and gradually brought the boat closer to the shore. The two bandits still did not notice. At this time, Qiu used his martial arts skills, jumped ashore, and ran away quickly, turning from bay to bay to avoid the bandits' eyes. When he saw electric lights flashing and the road was flat, he knew that he had reached the concession. The road was unusually quiet, and vehicles were rarely seen. Just as he was anxious, he suddenly saw a car company sign in front of him. He looked closely and saw that it was the Huaxin Linji Car Company at 354 Rue de la Tour. He rushed in and told the cashier the truth. The cashier, surnamed Wang, listened to him and knew that he was the famous actor Qiu Jianfei who had been kidnapped. However, all the cars at that time had been rented out. He used the telephone to borrow one from another company and sent Qiu home. When he arrived home, it was already late at night. Qiu, because he had been imprisoned in the bandits' den for half a month, a suffering he had never experienced in his life, set off yesterday to Suzhou and Wuxi for relaxation.

Englishman Charles Killed by Cook 142

A Tragic Case of Murder for Money

Charles Lived in Luxury

The Cook Suddenly Had Evil Thoughts

He Entered the Room at Midnight with a Kitchen Knife

He Was Seriously Wounded and Eventually Died

Charles, an Englishman, 53 years old, worked at the Customs. He lived with his wife on the third floor of a Western-style house at 859 North Sichuan Road. A week ago, his wife left him to return to her country. Charles lived alone. However, Charles was quite wealthy and liked to dress up. He usually wore luxurious clothes. The diamond ring on his finger, the gold watch on his wrist, the dazzling light, and the brilliant colors were envied by those who saw them. His pocket was never empty. He often had piles of banknotes, vaguely visible outside his clothes, which aroused the greed of bandits. Charles' cook, Xue Cheng, a Cantonese, hired an assistant named Pan Zhi half a month ago, who was also from Guangdong. Pan saw that his master was covered in treasures. In addition to coveting them,

He Had Evil Intentions and Had Long Wanted to Rob Him. There was no opportunity to take advantage of. Recently, he learned that the master was sleeping alone at night, thinking that he should not miss this opportunity. So, at 1:00 AM yesterday, he sneaked into the kitchen and took a sharp kitchen knife, carried it upstairs, and broke into Charles' room. Charles woke up from his dream and, with sleepy eyes, caught sight of

a Shiny Steel Knife and shouted for help. But Pan had already rushed towards him and slashed him in the face. Charles resisted with his bare hands, resulting in two cuts on his shoulders and arms. Pan also panicked, threw the knife, and ran downstairs to hide. Charles then

Shouted from the Window. At this time, detectives Feng Qi and Zhang Yuting from the Hongkou Police Station heard the alarm and rushed to the scene. Because the gate of the house was tightly closed, they did not wait for it to be opened and jumped in from the window on the side of the gate. They first went upstairs and saw Charles

lying in a Pool of Blood. After inquiring about the details, they immediately reported to the police station by telephone and searched the house for the murderer. The detectives thought that all the doors were closed, and they guessed that the murderer might be hiding in the house. Later, they found Pan

standing in a Corner near the kitchen toilet, with blood stains on the soles of his feet. They arrested him. At this time, Chief Inspector Heller from the Hongkou Police Station had already sent Western police officer No. 139 to arrive by car. They took Charles to the Suzhou Road Public Hospital for treatment and took Pan back to the police station for questioning and strict detention. It was already six o'clock in the morning. The detectives, because Pan confessed at the police station to

Murdering for Money and also said that Xue Cheng was also an accomplice, went to that place again. Xue was still wandering on the second floor, looking thoughtful, and was arrested. Later, at 8:00 AM, they were sent to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Ge Zhitan sat in the third courtroom for interrogation. However, the victim, Charles, died at 3:20 PM at the Public Hospital because the blood vessels in the injured area had been severed, resulting in

Excessive Blood Loss. The police lawyer, Wei Yinde, went to the court, explaining the previous situation, stating that Charles had died from his injuries, the murder weapon was still in the custody of the police station, and there were various aspects of the case that needed to be investigated, requesting an extension of the trial. Then, Chinese and Western detectives reported the circumstances of the arrest of the two defendants and stated that the deceased's bedroom

Had Been Sealed. Judge Ge then interrogated Pan Zhi, who confessed that he had conspired with Xue Cheng beforehand, and with Xue's consent, he had carried a kitchen knife upstairs last night at midnight and broke into the master's bedroom. Xue also held

a Short-Handled Axe and followed me into the room to provide support. I attacked the master's arm twice and then jumped out of the window and fled. We harmed the master to steal his money, etc. According to Xue Cheng's confession, he lived at 27 Baoshan Road, Baotong Road, Zhabei. I am employed at Charles' residence. Every night at 7:15 PM, I have to go home to stay overnight and go to work at the employer's place at 5:30 AM the next morning. Two weeks ago, I was chatting with a friend at an insurance company. The friend recommended Pan Zhi as my assistant. Now that his case of murdering for money has been discovered,

He Is Falsely Accusing Me. I know nothing about this matter. Moreover, the deceased treated me very well. How could I do such an illegal thing? Therefore, Pan's confession, which involves me, is all fabricated. Before I returned home last night, I even bought

Two Eggs because the master needed them for breakfast. Now these two eggs are still in the vegetable basket in the kitchen. This morning, I went to the master's place from my home and first looked for Pan, but I couldn't find him, so I went to the second floor. At that time, the detectives arrived and arrested me, etc. Judge Ge ordered Pan and Xue to be taken back into custody and adjourned the hearing to another date. Because the case was important, he personally went to 859 North Sichuan Road, third floor, with the clerk, at 3:00 PM to investigate the scene. At that time, the police also brought Pan and Xue, and Judge Ge asked in detail about the

Circumstances of the Murder. After the inspection, he returned to the court, and Pan and Xue were taken back to the police station for custody by the police. As for Charles' remains, the police car took them to the Philanthropic Road morgue, reported to the British Consular Court, and a judge was specially dispatched to verify the identity and collect the remains.

Wenhui News reported that Charles Goddard, the deputy head of the foreign clerks of the Customs, was cut by a cook and died at the Public Hospital. This morning (19th), Anderson, the coroner of the British Consular Court, went to the hospital to examine the body. Bras, a Westerner from the Customs, testified that he had known the deceased for sixteen years and knew that he had no disputes over finances or family affairs before his death. The deceased had served in the Customs for twenty-five years and left a wife who is now in Hong Kong. After the interrogating officer finished asking, he ordered an extension of the hearing to next Saturday at the British Public Hall.

Sentencing of Zhu Jixing's Case 143

Sentenced to Four Years of Imprisonment

Zhu Jixing, the deputy compradore of the Chartered Bank, embezzled more than 160,000 taels of silver from the bank's accounts and abandoned his post to flee. The Chartered Bank also accused the accountants Xie Tonghou and Yu Xiling of colluding in fraud. The police successively arrested the three and interrogated them to the end, and the sentence was pending. This has been reported in this newspaper many times. Yesterday morning, the date for the sentencing arrived. Judge Xu took the bench and ordered Zhu and others to be brought forward. The lawyer representing the Chartered Bank stood up before the sentencing and stated that regarding the civil suit part of the case, the defendant had previously offered to reconcile with the plaintiff, but there had been no indication of reconciliation. He should be noted. Judge Xu then announced the sentence: Zhu Jixing was sentenced to four years of imprisonment, and the number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized would be commuted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Xie Tonghou was fined 300 yuan. If he could not pay, he would be allowed to commute one day of imprisonment for every three yuan. Yu Xiling was found not guilty. The forty forged bank notes were confiscated. The civil suit part will be transferred to the civil court for handling.

Li Zaocheng Lost His Life Because of His Beautiful Wife 144

The Result of a Love Triangle

Two Suspects Arrested

At 1:30 AM yesterday morning, a shooting occurred in Tanziawan, Zhabei. The deceased was Li Zaocheng, the owner of the Tongxing Tea Garden in that area. The reason was jealousy and resentment, involving a love triangle. The circumstances were very complicated. The murderers, Shen Changgen and Fei Deji, fled without a trace after the incident. Only two suspects were arrested. The details are as follows:

Possessing a Beautiful and Charming Wife, Li Zaocheng (also known as Li Dazaozi), from Yancheng, is 31 years old and owns the Tongxing Tea Garden at 355 Caopeng, Tanziawan, Zhabei. The business is booming and can be called a small fortune. His brother, Decheng, is a rice shop runner. They live separately, renting houses in 16 Hengyu Lane, Hengfeng Road. Although they live in different places, they often visit each other. The brotherly relationship is very close. His wife, Zhao, maiden name Ayin, is 20 years old and has good looks. They have been married for less than half a year. The couple's love is as deep as the sea. Li cherishes her like a precious jewel. Who would have thought that Li's assassination was caused by this? If Li knew, he would not be able to rest in peace.

The Woman Had Two Lovers Before. Shen Changgen, who owns the Xiexing Land Goods Store, is already married. He used to be fond of Zhao and insisted on marrying her as a concubine. She secretly communicated with him and was very close, but she was unwilling to be a concubine and never agreed to marry him. Shen said that he must achieve his goal. She saw that he was stubborn and began to hate him. She abandoned him and fell in love with Fei Deji, leaving Shen behind. Unexpectedly, after a few months, her mother suddenly betrothed her to Li Zaocheng, and she married into the family in February of this year. From then on, her two lovers were unable to contact her.

The Thought of Revenge Arose. Although Shen and Fei were rejected by her, they still could not forget her. They often went to Li's teahouse to drink tea, but she ignored them. The two were filled with anger, and the thought of revenge arose. After discussing it for many days, they decided to kill her and her husband to be satisfied.

Unforeseen Bullet Flying over. At 1:30 AM yesterday morning, Li and she were just enjoying their dreams when they suddenly heard a knock on the door. Li's employee, Yang Zhanyuan, got up and opened the door. Unexpectedly, three rough men suddenly broke in, saying that the boss was there. There were three more people guarding outside the door, looking around, looking very dangerous. When Yang heard this, he knew that the comers were not good people. One of them took out a pistol, forbidding him to make a sound. Yang saw the weapon and retreated to a corner, trembling. Then two people walked into the room. Li had already woken up and was about to go out to see, but an merciless bullet hit his head, and he fell down. The murderers knew that they had caused trouble and fled in all directions.

Zaocheng Died. When Zhao saw Zaocheng lying in a pool of blood, she touched him and found that he was dead. She was shocked and reported to the Tanziawan police station in the fourth district. She also ordered someone to inform her brother Li Decheng. Chief Shi led the police to search for them, but the murderers had long disappeared. He reported back to the headquarters and asked for their arrest.

Two Suspects were Arrested. Chief Jin, upon receiving the report, immediately ordered Police Officer Gong to go with the investigators to arrest them. Two suspects, Hou Afu and Ruan Rusheng, were arrested and brought to the station. After questioning, they were detained for investigation. The corpse was inspected by Prosecutor Lei in the afternoon. It was determined that the cause of death was a gunshot wound. He ordered the family of the deceased to prepare a coffin for burial.

Selling a Five-Year-Old Boy for Only Ten Yuan 145

Because of Lack of Travel Expenses

Sent to the Public Security Bureau for Relief

At 1:00 PM yesterday, a middle-aged woman brought a four or five-year-old boy to the Pudong Lan Ni Du Pier and asked to sell him, saying that the price was only ten yuan. A large crowd gathered to watch. The patrolling police arrived at the scene and took the woman and the child to the Third District of the Public Security Bureau. The woman confessed that her name was Chen Li, 31 years old, from Lishui. Her husband was doing hat business in Ningbo, and there had been no news from home for a long time. So she went to Ningbo ten days ago to look for him, but she could not find him. She passed through Shanghai, and her travel expenses were exhausted. She had no choice but to sell her own five-year-old son, and there was no other reason. The district chief thought that selling children was against humanity and sent them to the Public Security Bureau for relief.

The Municipal Public Works Bureau Urges San Yi Lane to Improve Its Artesian Well 146

San Yi Lane on Qiujiang Road, Zhabei, has an artesian well to supply drinking water to the tenants. The Municipal Public Works Bureau has repeatedly urged improvement because of the unclean water quality and insufficient water volume. Recently, it was reported that the well has been short of water since summer, which is very inconvenient for the residents to drink. The bureau sent personnel to investigate on July 16. According to the residents, there is no water at all from 11:00 AM to 2:00 PM every day, and the water flow is also slow at other times, especially in the south of the lane. The officer tried to open the faucet and found that no water flowed out. The bureau believes that drinking water is a daily necessity for human life and is especially urgent in this hot summer. It sent a letter to the owner, San Yi Company, the day before yesterday, ordering them to improve it within a time limit. If it is impossible to improve it, they should connect to the Zhabei tap water to improve hygiene.

Bondholders of China and Foreign Telephone Company Discuss the Issue of Redemption of Bonds 147

The China Press reported that the bondholders of the Shanghai China and Foreign Telephone Company held a meeting yesterday (18th) at the board room of the Yangtze Insurance Company to discuss the company's early redemption of bonds. Chairman Hobbrow stated that the 7% bonds must be redeemed by December 21, 1933, according to the regulations. At present, the Shanghai securities interest rate may be lower than 7% (that is, the interest rate of the bonds), so to compensate the bondholders for the loss of reinvestment, the redemption price should be increased. He immediately proposed that if the company redeems each bond with a face value of 100 taels at 103 taels before the end of this year, and the interest is calculated up to the date of redemption, then it can be allowed to redeem it. This was unanimously approved by the attendees. The company issued a total of 1.5 million taels of bonds. On that day, creditors with 624,000 taels of bonds attended.

The French Concession Will Reorganize the Fire Brigade 148

Fire Expert Kerner Arrives in Shanghai

The China Press reported that the French Concession authorities, in order to reorganize the fire brigade in the concession, recently hired Captain Kerner, a fire expert from Paris, to serve as the captain. Kerner arrived in Shanghai yesterday (14th) on the Dada Nanyang steamship and will take office within a few days. His wife and daughter also came on the same ship. From now on, the firefighters of the French Concession will be completely changed to professional occupations, paid salaries, and there will be no more voluntary members. The reorganization is already underway and is expected to be fully completed by the end of this year.

It was not until yesterday morning when the body floated up that they found out. A Sand Boat Encountered Robbers in the Waters of Wenzhou 156

One of the Crew Members was Kidnapped

The sand boat Shunlongxing, fully loaded with South Seas products (collectively known as South Goods) from Fujian Province, was transporting them to Shanghai this time. Unexpectedly, when traveling through the waters near Wenzhou, Zhejiang Province, several boats resembling fishing boats suddenly came sailing from behind. Cheng Baoxing, the captain of the sand boat, saw that the situation was strange and knew that he had encountered robbers. At that time, the south wind was very strong, so he immediately instructed the crew to pull up the sails as much as possible, hoping to escape. However, the robber boats opened fire in the rear, knocking down the helmsman, and the boat was skewed and unstable. At this time, the robber boats had arrived and surrounded the Shunlongxing sand boat. The robbers, holding weapons, swarmed aboard, about twenty or more, drove the crew into the stern, and sent robbers to guard them. The gold boat was searched and robbed of more than 230 yuan in silver dollars, and all the goods were moved to the robber boats, resulting in huge losses. Before leaving, they searched the crew members, kidnapped one crew member (the robbers thought he was the captain), broke the rudder, and then fired their guns and gathered their team to leave. Afterwards, the sand boat repaired the rudder and did not arrive in Shanghai until yesterday. Captain Cheng Baoxing went to various cargo shops to report the robbery situation, waited to find out the number of robbed goods, opened a list to report to the Maritime Public Security Team and the Naval Headquarters, and asked for their arrest. The injured helmsman was sent to the hospital for treatment.

The Case of Xiao Yang Yuelou's Stolen and Pawned Costumes 157

His Assistant Sentenced to Two Months Imprisonment

Yang Huinong, also known as Xiao Yang Yuelou, a performer residing at No. 12 Renchang Lane, Route Cardinal Foch, in the French Concession, had his stage costumes repeatedly stolen and pawned by his assistant, Xu Chengfo, over the past year. Only recently did Yang discover this and report it to the French police. Detective Cai Lian'gen apprehended Xu and recovered some of the stolen goods. Yesterday, Xu was brought before the French court for prosecution. The plaintiff, Yang, detailed the previous events, stating that the stolen costumes were worth a total of 924 silver dollars, with over 190 silver dollars already pawned. He explained that he had hired the defendant as his assistant some years ago, and initially, everything was fine, so he trusted him. However, later, he became addicted to opium, and his earnings were insufficient to cover his expenses. As a result, he repeatedly stole costumes to pawn. At first, Yang was unaware, as Xu would pawn other costumes to redeem the ones needed for the day. Day after day, the debts grew, and eventually, he could no longer redeem the costumes and fled. Now that he has been apprehended, Yang requested a trial. Xu Chengfo confessed that he committed the crimes because Yang Huinong was ill and lacked funds, leaving him no choice but to resort to illegal actions and begged for leniency. Judge Zhu sentenced Xu to two months in the Western Jail as a warning, and the recovered costumes were returned to the plaintiff.

Damaging a Big Cake Shop's Stove

Injuring a Rickshaw Puller's Foot

The driver of a cargo truck, Chen Jingou, was driving along Caojiadu Road in western Shanghai the afternoon before yesterday when a child suddenly jumped in front of the vehicle. Boat Crewman's Right Leg Crushed 159

Ding Xuelin, a wheat boatman, recently arrived in Shanghai from Qingjiao with 300 dan of wheat to be unloaded at the Northern City Flour Mill. Yesterday, while waiting for the tide at the southern entrance of Rihui Port, Ding's crew member, Xinggen, was washing clothes on the bow of the boat. A Pinghu ship approached, also waiting for the tide to dock. Due to careless steering, the Pinghu ship collided with the bow of Ding's boat. Xinggen could not avoid the collision, and his right leg was crushed between the two ships, causing him to faint from the excruciating pain and bleed profusely. The crew of the Pinghu ship, realizing they had caused the accident, fled south. Ding's crew hired a small boat and chased after them. Meanwhile, Ding took Xinggen to the Northern City Hospital. It was reported that his leg was severed and he was permanently disabled, but his life was saved. The Pinghu ship was caught near Dujiahang, and the ship owner was arrested and taken to the police station for investigation.

The Shanghai Medical Journal Press, located in Shipi Lane inside the West Gate of Shanghai, was established by prominent Shanghai traditional Chinese medicine practitioners. Its publication, the Shanghai Medical Journal, aims to promote Chinese medicine and its theories. It has already published over seventy issues. Letters 169

To the Editor,

I recently read in your newspaper's local news column on the 18th that there were two "steelworks reform crucible" stories. The so-called reform plan did not fully match the facts, and also leading to the funding to purchase firebricks was not based on anything. As for the manufacture of bombs, the situation has been reported and has not yet been instructed to follow. Whether the plant is open or not, the plant is also unknown. I'm afraid it may confuse the rumors, so I have sent it to you, and I hope to make corrections to the Shuzhao Fact. Sincerely, Shanghai Steel Factory, July 19,

To the Editor,

A news item, "The Ministry of Finance Orders the Municipal Finance Bureau to Release Funds" (this news item was submitted by the New Shanghai News Agency) was published in your newspaper's local news column. After reviewing the content, it was completely untrue. The various municipal taxes collected by our bureau are local revenue, and all are used for local expenditures, such as municipal administrative expenses and various construction projects, etc. There are budget regulations, and they are directly received and paid by the municipal treasury. It does not need to be handed over to the national treasury as an example. The Ministry of Finance mentioned in your newspaper has never received any such ministry order, and I don't know what it is based on. I am very surprised. I am afraid that rumors will confuse the audience. I would like to ask you to check and make corrections immediately. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance, July 19,

A Laughing Matter Hai Ke 170

Young Man: Mr. Old Gentleman. I certainly have seen you before.

Old Gentleman: Perhaps so. Because I have been the Warden of the local prison for twenty years.

Father: My son. I am already old. You are already twenty-five years old. You should try to support yourself. You must not rely on me for a lifetime. What will you do when your mother and I are gone?

Son: It doesn't matter. I can go to an orphanage.

A: What are you saying? Am I a fool with no intelligence or knowledge?

B: You are always right. How dare I argue with you?

Teacher: Children. Alcohol is harmful. You must never drink alcohol. You must treat it as an enemy.

Student: Then we should love it. Doesn't the Bible say, "Love your enemies"?

Man: Darling. Please go further away. Don't come near me.

Woman: Why? Do I have thorns on my body?

Man: No. It's just that when I look at your beautiful eyes, the fire of love in my heart will burn.

Woman: What are you afraid of? The fire brigade is right across the street.

Small Notes from the Melon Pot Studio Zhi Yuan 171

The poem of the secluded wind says, "Eat melons in July, break gourds in August." July and August in the Zhou dynasty correspond to May and June in the summer. The weather is extremely hot. Avoid eating fishy and fatty foods. Dig bamboo shoots and cut vegetables. They have a special and refined taste. In the countryside, people gather under bean trellises and melon vines for evening talks. The sound of cicadas accompanies them, and fireflies seem to flow. It is a wonderful picture of escaping the summer heat.

Guang Ya lists dragon hooves, beast paws, variegated sheep, rabbit heads, cinnamon marrow, honey tubes, small green, and large class as names for melons. However, there are two types of melons. Those used in cooking, such as winter melon and loofah, are large and called "gua." Small ones are called "die." Those like gourds and are all of that category. Emperor Xiaowu of the Song dynasty wrote in a poem, "Climbing sauce to season autumn vegetables," referring to pickled cucumbers. Lu You wrote in a poem, "Sunny days expose pickled cucumbers," referring to salted cucumbers. To eat them with breakfast or drink with wine in the evening, is something that only people with refined taste can appreciate. As for watermelons and other types, they are only for relieving heat and are probably not suitable for inclusion in a menu.

Gourds are a type of melon. They are long and have a stem. "Hu" is also written as "hulu." In fact, it is "hu." Bitter gourds are bitter and sweet gourds are sweet. Tao Hongjing once said this. Zhengzitong says that "hu" is also called. In the past, Lu Huaixin entertained guests and told the cook, "Steam until tender, remove the hair, and don't break the neck." The listeners thought it was steamed duck. But when the lid was lifted, it was just steamed gourd. However, if the fruit is peeled and seeds removed, and cut into short segments, seasoned with salt, the fragrance is refreshing. Or cut into thin strips and mixed with dried bamboo shoots, it is also quite delicious. But people in Fujian and Guangdong prefer to eat sweet gourds and bitter gourds. It is probably what is called the different tastes of different people.

The Food and Goods Chronicle of the Former Han Dynasty says, "Vegetables are grown in fields, melons and gourds are grown. Old farmers can always taste the new crops." The melons and gourds in Shanghai are carried from villages by only 30-40%. The rest are bundled and carried from other places. After one night or two nights, all the essence is gone. But the price is almost the same as fish and meat. I am ashamed to be a poor scholar and have been gnawing on vegetable roots for a long time. How can I return to Wuxing and look for the land of purple and yellow eggplants?

Fragments of Hangzhou Travel (Middle) Huang Jiping 172

The next morning at ten o'clock, Mr. Ge's first lecture was entitled "The Past, Present, and Future of Newspapers." First, he placed historical materials of newspapers on the wall, such as the first Chinese newspaper run by foreigners during the Jiaqing period. The earliest single-sided and double-sided printing

Strange Tales of Turtle's Cry Ji Jin 173

A family surnamed Wang in Xiaxiang, Wuzhen, in the lake district, raised a turtle. It was nearly a hundred years old and had nothing special about it. One day last month, the owner took a boat to Shanghai. Just as he went out, the turtle suddenly raised its head and cried, chirping and squeaking like a chick looking for food. Everyone was surprised. Listeners gathered from all directions. It only stopped after about half an hour. The owner was suddenly urged to leave, but there was not enough time. He knew it was because of the turtle. He was very angry and ordered his family to throw it into the river. It sank and floated, and no one knew where it went.

At that time, there were many discussions. Everyone thought that there would be more bad luck than good. The owner had always been known as a reformer and did not believe in superstition. He listened to it and that was it. One day he got an alarm and learned that the boat had arrived near Luxu last night. Suddenly, it encountered bandits. Luggage and valuables were robbed. Many passengers were shot. Then he realized that the turtle was crying to save him. Overjoyed, he sent someone to the original place to find a way to retrieve it. But it had sunk into the sea. It is not known whether it can be returned to its owner. Mr. Xu, a neighbor in the same village, said this with certainty. So I have recorded it.

Prints. Various major newspapers before and after the Guangxu Restoration were all items that were not easily seen in a hundred years. Some were taken by Mr. Ge at the British Museum. There were more than fifty listeners, who were all colleagues in the newspaper industry. They all felt very interested. On the morning of the 3rd, the second lecture was "An Overview of the World Newspaper Industry Today." He first displayed illustrated magazines from various countries. Some were monochrome, some were three-color. All were newly printed with photogravure. It was a dazzling array. He also had maps of the communication networks of Reuters, United, and Dentsu. When he spoke of the development of the newspaper industry and news agencies in various countries and the backwardness of our country's propaganda, the listeners were all moved. On the evening of the 4th, the third lecture was "The Awakening that the Chinese Newspaper Industry Should Have." He also showed slides, showing the internal and external conditions of newspaper offices in various countries. More than a hundred people attended. The meeting only ended at midnight. After the three lectures, the Hangzhou newspaper industry deeply felt the difficulty of their own work and the difficulty of life. They asked Mr. Ge for ways to solve the problem. From this, it can be seen that the colleagues' desire to make progress is deep and sincere.

There are six newspapers in Hangzhou. They are the Minguo Daily, the Guomin News, the Zhijiang Daily, the Zhemin Daily, the Minsheng News, and the Zhejiang Business Daily. We have made a survey of them. Among them, the Minguo has a larger scale. The rest are simple and crude. Printing is also outsourced. Two sheets are published daily, and some are three. The editing is still good. In terms of news, it is all the same. There are few original articles that are worth reading. According to a gentleman with a long history in the newspaper industry, the advertising revenue of each newspaper is not abundant. The one with the most sales is over 3,000. All feel strapped for cash in terms of economics. Reporters are treated very poorly, so it is difficult to find many who are clean and self-respecting. Printing workers are even more difficult to deal with. In fact, the above points are not only the common disease of the inland newspaper industry, but also the metropolitan newspaper is similar. I hope that both labor and capital will do their best and gradually improve to promote progress together.

After arriving in Hangzhou, friends treated me to banquets almost every day. During one banquet, I talked about Hangzhou's prohibition of smoking, gambling, and prostitution, as well as the situation of bandits in Zhejiang. I heard from the elders that since the strict prohibition of smoking and gambling, there have been achievements. Social crimes have decreased invisibly. This is truly one aspect of the provincial government's achievements. However, it is not easy to sweep away all the accumulated malpractices of the evil society. Taking Hangzhou as an example, smoking and gambling seem to have been banned on the surface, but in reality they are still present. For example, public prostitutes have closed down, but private prostitutes have emerged. The authorities ban prostitutes by drawing lots. The women who have left the human flesh market are temporarily placed in shelters. At first, they did not feel bitter. Later, because of the difficulty of life and the hopelessness of marriage, they were unwilling to stay for a long time. Some came out and became private prostitutes again. This is because the authorities have failed to provide a thorough solution. Opium can still be found in hotels and apartments, where people can lie on a couch and smoke freely. Due to the police's lack of effort, red pills are now popular. People in the underworld use them to get high. According to reports, red pills are Japanese goods. Their poison is more potent than opium. Those who are addicted to them can die within two years. Banditry is frequently heard in Zhejiang. Newspapers rarely record it. The authorities use the old trick of covering their ears and stealing bells. It is not a good idea. I also heard from a gentleman who had just returned to Hangzhou from Hanzhao that opium is publicly sold in Wuhan and Hanyang. Prostitution and gambling are allowed. The two lakes special tax office only cares about a large amount of revenue and does not ask about anything else. It is regrettable.

A Record of Anecdotes About Lu Huanyan Ji Jin 174

It was reported that Lu Huanyan, deputy commander of the Eighth Route Army and chairman of the Guangxi Provincial Government, was unfortunately assassinated in the middle of last month. Critics lamented his loss. Now a friend has come from Guilin and told me two anecdotes about him that are rarely known and have not been mentioned in the newspapers. I will record them here to help you.

Whispers from the East (12) Qian Hua 175

(10) The Press in Tokyo

Tokyo is the political center of Japan. Since the Great Kanto Earthquake of the twelfth year of the Taisho era, the government and the people have worked together on reconstruction. To this day, it has largely succeeded. All buildings and city plans are being carried out according to the latest ideal city designs. Its prosperity is comparable to the world's largest metropolises such as New York, London, Paris, and Berlin. After arriving in Tokyo from Osaka on the 16th, I, as a reporter, prepared day and night for the news coverage of the conference. In my spare time, I took some tours. Regarding the various facilities of the Japanese people and the rapid advancement of their undertakings, I could only repeatedly praise them and couldn't add a single word. There is not a single thing I have seen in Tokyo that is not worth recording. But the threads are so tangled that I don't know where to start. As a reporter speaking about the press, I will first describe the press in Tokyo. The newspaper industry in Japan is currently in a golden age. There are a total of 513 newspapers nationwide, excluding 27 in Korea and 4 in Taiwan. The flourishing state of the Osaka Asahi and Mainichi Shimbun described in the previous article is not a special case in one place, but a crystallization of universal development. Education is widespread among the Japanese people, even rickshaw drivers hold newspapers in their hands and read them along the way. Moreover, the public has extremely sophisticated discernment, and newspapers with a slight slant are rejected. Therefore, newspapers such as Asahi and Mainichi are purely neutral and fulfill their responsibility as the mouthpiece of the people. Newspapers with a slant are mostly run by political parties such as the Minseito and Seiyukai. As for openly receiving subsidies from the government, that is almost non-existent. In areas where local newspapers are thriving, there are often more than ten, or at least two or three. Their operating income is sufficient for self-sufficiency. However, some larger and more profitable ones, such as the Fukuoka Nichinichi Shimbun, have a capital of one million yuan and sell hundreds of thousands of copies daily, earning hundreds of thousands of yuan annually. The Kobe Shimbun has a capital of 400,000 yuan, and its sales and profits are also over 100,000, enough to dominate one area. Japanese newspapers all operate evening editions, so there is no gap in the news. If there is any important news, an extra is issued, costing one or two copper coins. Evening editions also sell for two copper coins. Newsboys sell them along the way and sell out in an instant. There are 22 daily newspapers and 42 news agencies in Tokyo. The Tokyo Asahi Shimbun, Tokyo Nichinichi Shimbun, and Tokyo Mainichi Shimbun have a newspaper capital of over 300,000 yuan and sales of over 100,000 copies. , Hochi Shimbun, Yomiuri Shimbun, Chugai Commercial News, Jiji Shinpō, Miyako Shimbun, Kokumin Shimbun, Yorozu Chōhō, Tokyo Every

Evening News, Tokyo Taisei Shimbun, and the English-language Japan Times. Among the news agencies, the larger ones include the Japan Telegraphic Communication Agency, with a capital of one million yuan, the Japan News Agency with 500,000 yen, the Nikkan Chuo News Agency with a capital of 500,000 yuan, the Insurance Nichinichi News Agency with a capital of 100,000 yuan, the Tokyo News Agency with a capital of 100,000 yuan, the Toyokuni News Agency with a capital of 200,000 yuan, the Day and Night News Agency with a capital of 100,000 yuan, the News United News Agency, the Naiwai News Agency with a capital of 500,000 yuan, and the Imperial News Agency with a capital of 500,000 yuan.

Lü Xing was upright and had a chivalrous spirit. He was poor in his youth and often lived with relatives. One day, he returned from the school and passed by a teahouse. He saw a fortune teller beckoning him to sit down and said to him, "Your appearance is extraordinary, with a tiger's jaw and a swallow's neck. You are definitely a person like Wei Qing and Huo Qubing. However, your Huagai star is too low, and you have very little fortune." Lü smiled and said, "My family is as poor as can be. I am lucky to avoid freezing and starvation. How dare I have any hope?" He left without paying attention. A tea guest in the seat had inherited a hundred plots of land, but it was seized by a powerful man. He had been suing for a long time without success. Hearing the fortune teller's words, he spent money to help Lü and persuaded him to study at the Army Lecture Hall in the provincial capital. He also said, "If you become noble in the future, I beg you to help with this matter. I dare not hope for anything else." Lü reluctantly agreed. In a few years, he graduated from the examination and was assigned as a company commander in a certain battalion. He entered and exited military gates and had some power. He immediately wrote a letter to the county magistrate, ordering the return of the land to the guest. The guest was endlessly grateful to him. After Lü was promoted to division commander, he became even stricter with his subordinates. If anything displeased him, he would scold them at every turn. None of his subordinates dared to disobey him in the slightest. One day, he was playing chess with a certain councilor. Halfway through the game, he suddenly got up and went inside. The councilor sat and waited for a long time, feeling very hungry. However, he did not dare to leave rashly. A guard entered to report, "The councilor is still here. We should give him lunch." Lü scolded, "What lunch? Eating my cannon is enough for him!" He was angry because he was losing the chess game. Such events were common. Some said that Lü's character was cruel and ungrateful, which was enough to bring about his own death.

Special Announcement: Yesterday, we received a telegram from Mr. Wu Kunyi of our Hangzhou branch, saying that a literary friend, Mr. Tang Meixi, committed suicide by taking an anesthetic potion in a certain room at the West Lake Hotel the night before last. He was discovered the next morning and rushed to the Hangzhou Hospital for treatment. His life can be saved without danger. Please notify his relatives, etc. Hearing the news, we were shocked and terrified. Because we do not know the whereabouts of Mr. Tang's relatives, we are publishing this notice to inform them. We hope they will go to the Hangzhou Hospital to visit him. Respectfully, Shou Juan.

Communications from the East (13) Wu Xiaohou 176

(Shen) Facilities for Tokyo's Electrical Business are Improving Daily. As an island nation, Japan relies on hydroelectric power generation. Throughout the country, all industries, commerce, and machinery use electricity as a driving force. Supply even exceeds demand. National statistics suggest there may be a surplus of electrical power. From Tokyo to Yokohama, in addition to railway trains powered by electricity, including door opening and closing, four electric tram tracks are also installed, reaching Yokohama directly. Moreover, the entire city, in addition to ordinary trams running on city streets, also has elevated trams and subway trams. Ordinary trams only have first-class seating, unlike the Tianjin-Shanghai trams in our China, which have first, second, and third class. However, the seating is spacious and clean. The tram depots are also lined with green flanges. Traveling within the city, regardless of distance, costs only seven sen per person, equivalent to seven fen in Japanese currency. Travel outside the city incurs a slight additional fee depending on the distance. Students from various schools who purchase monthly passes with their school certificates also receive special discounts. The electrical facilities can be roughly divided into three categories. (1) Electricity Supply: In addition to electric railways, electric tramways, and factory engines, the annual electricity supply for lighting in Tokyo and its 12 surrounding villages and towns is provided to 152,308 households. The total number of lights is 1,090,903. The power is over 45,000 horsepower. The total cost of all electric lights, power, wiring, and equipment is 7,963,162 yuan. (2) Power Equipment: Currently, Tokyo has the Tokyo Railway Co., Ltd., the Electric Power Co., Ltd., and the Tokyo Electric Light Co., Ltd. engaged in electric railway and electricity supply businesses. After the Great Kanto Earthquake on September 1, 1923, most of these were destroyed. These companies actively engaged in reconstruction. Construction began in 1926 and was completed in November 1928. Except for a large part of the railway being a state-run enterprise, the Electric Power Co., Ltd. spent as much as 180 million yuan, and the Tokyo Electric Light Co., Ltd. spent as much as 60 million yuan. (3) Tokyo Municipal Electrical Research Institute: Tokyo's electric railway and electricity supply businesses require thorough research in scientific and economic aspects. Necessary knowledge is essential for perfect implementation. This institute was established with funding from the Tokyo Electric Light Co., Ltd.'s survey and research organization in 1921. The construction of the building began in 1923. After the Great Earthquake, it was vigorously pursued, taking two and a half years and costing over 1.2 million yuan. The Tokyo Municipal Electrical Research Institute was fully established in October 1925. Currently, the important tasks of the institute include six items: (1) Electrical instrument testing. (2) Electrical appliance testing. (3) Research and investigation of electrical relations. (4) Patent registration. (5) Electrical museum. (6) Patent implementation and related manufacturing.

(You) Compilation and Statistical Survey of the History of Tokyo: Tokyo's process of national capital transformation and the difficulties of centuries of construction projects are of great historical significance. In October 1901, the Tokyo Municipal Assembly passed a resolution to establish a compilation committee, initiating the investigation and compilation of system evolution. After several evolutions and reforms, a concrete and detailed planning and statistics were developed. The municipal history is classified into fifteen chapters. The first chapter is a general record of the history of Tokyo. Chapters two through fifteen are divided into records of the city's land, municipal administration, city industry, city transportation, city education, city religion, city sanitation, city military affairs, city relief, city literature and art, city customs, city diplomacy, city history, and a city development chronology. This is the classification of the municipal history compilation. For municipal surveys, fifteen series are planned for compilation. The first series is on urban administrative organization. The second series is a general overview of municipal administration. The third to fourteenth series cover twelve aspects of administration: finance, education, social health, industry, roads, waterworks, sewers, river ports, parks, electricity, and public enterprises. The fifteenth series is on district administration. Of these fifteen series, only the first, fourth, and fifth series have been published. The rest are still being compiled or are still under investigation. In addition, the liaison for urban surveys and statistics is the Right Metropolitan Survey and Statistics Association. Its important functions are five: (1) Comparative survey of financial administration in major cities. (2) Survey on increasing efficiency in urban administrative affairs. (3) Unification of urban statistical survey items and methods. (4) Compilation of comparative statistical yearbooks for six major cities. (5) Comparative survey of public enterprises in major cities.

Financial Bar Gold Plummets Seven Taels 177

Spot prices plummet in a falling market, breaking the barrier. Yesterday, the 19th, the decline in bar gold intensified, having already broken the 600 tael barrier. Initially, it was still stable, but then it fell sharply, with a fluctuation of nearly ten taels in half a day. Foreign exchange was weakening, with little activity in bank transactions, and although market trading was brisk, the psychology of the industry was weak, with selling generally exceeding buying. Hengxing, Yuanmao, Yongfu, Xingyong, Yu Da, Da Yong, Da, etc. all sold, while Fuchang, Yuancheng, Yongzhi, Fengyong, etc. bought. Since the morning market was low, it was mediocre. As buyers became strong, it became firm, now seen around 606 taels. In the future, exchange rates seem to be loosening, and large households are inclined to sell. Spot goods are especially quiet, and prices are also declining. Futures, forced by the environment, suddenly turned down and fell sharply by almost ten taels, plummeting to around 596 taels. The market will be closed over the weekend as usual. Yesterday, the Bank of England fell by 1/8, the forward rate by 1/16, and the Bank of America by 1/8.

Initially stable, but eventually falling steadily. September gold opened slightly up by 8 cents, at 604 taels. It then fell by 5 or 6 cents, but with Fuchang, Zhifengyong buying, it rose by 2, 3 or 4 cents, reaching 5 taels and 8 cents. The first order was revealed, and the listed price did not change, so it fell to 4 taels and 3 cents. In a moment, it rose and fell slightly by 1 tael, and the internal first order was fixed. Banks were mutually doing July at 6 pence 125, and Citibank was doing September at 37 yuan, reaching 605 taels at 10:00. Later, July was doing 6 pence 1875, August 25, and Hengxing, Yu Da, Yuanmao, Yong, etc. were all selling, and the price was getting lower and lower. Soon, the 600 tael barrier was broken. Around 11:00, it was 599 taels. At that time, it was replenished by small households, and it returned to 600 taels and 8 cents. After 11:15, the selling sentiment of large households such as Yongda, Fuxing, and Yongbingxing was strong, causing the market to become even more sluggish, with almost no chance of recovery. The 600 tael barrier was broken again, but although foreign exchange was weakening, trading was idle. By 11:30, it was only 97 taels. After a short time, it recovered by about 2 taels, but sellers were incessant. Because the market is closed today (Sunday), those who previously held long positions were eager to level out, and it fell again by 2 taels. By noon, it closed at 596 taels and 2 cents, a decrease of 7 taels compared to the previous day. It has fallen for three consecutive days, totaling 9 taels. The highest price in the previous market was 605 taels and 8 cents, and the lowest price was 596 taels and 2 cents, a difference of 9 taels and 6 cents. The listed price was still 657 taels. The initial press was 52 and 3 taels, and at noon it was suppressed by more than 60 taels. The accounts for July and August were 95 taels, September was 96 taels, the replenishment was 95 taels, the opening price for goods was 603 taels and 7 cents, and the noon closing price was 596 taels.

Industry psychology is negative, and they concentrate on selling. Hengxing, Yuanmao Yong, Bingxing, Yongda, Yu Da, and Fuxingyong had the most transactions. Changshengyong, Yuanheng, Xinheng, and Yuxingyong all sold in the morning. Dadecheng, Zhifengyong, Wanxing, and Shunli had irregular ups and downs. Flour Standard and Inland Merchants Continuously Sell Off 190

Yesterday's flour market showed weakness in all months after the opening. Although foreign wheat quotations rebounded by 4, 5, 6, or 7 jiao, overall market sentiment did not improve significantly. This is because the inland merchants (mostly from Wuxi) believe that early-maturing wheat will soon be harvested, and reports from various places indicate a good harvest, with 80-90% certainty of a bumper crop. Therefore, those who previously intended to buy high have now changed their attitude due to the environment, either closing their long positions or engaging in short selling, especially in the distant months. Looking ahead, if actual sales remain sluggish, it should weaken further. As a result, the current month was down by 2.5 li compared to the previous day, August was down by 7.5 li, October was down by 1 fen, November was down by 1.25 fen, and December was down by 1 fen.

However, when the market opened in the afternoon, the flour market weakened again, and market sentiment was affected. Given the changed environment, the future outlook remains unfavorable.
