Social News

Experiment on the Breathing Rate of Women 197

Regarding the breathing of women, French doctors had previously made reports on their tests. However, women cultivated in modern life have naturally undergone changes. Recently, Francis G. Benedict of New York, USA, published the results of his research over the years. Although it is a small discovery, it has attracted attention from the European and American scientific communities. According to his report, women breathe three to five times per minute, with the strongest women as the standard for testing. At most, it is only six to eight times. He obtained the results two years ago, but still thought it was not enough to be credible. This year, he traveled to Europe to give lectures and conduct tests, and the results were the same. Therefore, he recently formally published his results to the scientific community, which is considered to be of great help to doctors specializing in women's diseases and pharmacists in their formulations. (Yi Kang)

The Future of European and American Air Routes 198

Although there have been several long-distance flights across the Atlantic between Europe and America, they have all been trials and have not carried passengers or transported mail. In this era of increasing progress in European and American civilization, it still takes many days to travel from the United States to Europe, which many people feel is inconvenient. According to recent German newspaper reports, the plan for a commercial airline across the Atlantic between Europe and America has gradually become a reality after several years of planning. The air route goes from Baltimore in the central United States to Seirle in Spain, from where it can be connected to major European cities by land flights. For safety reasons, an airport will be set up on Bermuda Island in the Atlantic Ocean for practical use. The cost of air travel from the United States to Spain is twice the cost of a ship, but the time required is only two days. The return trip from Spain to the United States is also only three days. There will be a total of four aircraft. In addition to the German Graf Zeppelin, three new aircraft will need to be built. Two of them are being manufactured by the U.S. Navy Department in Akron, and the remaining one is being manufactured in Germany. The equipment used has never been used in aircraft before. The estimated opening date is set for 1932. (Yi Kang)

United States Invents New Machine Gun 199

The United States Navy Department recently accepted a huge machine gun. The gun was created by Robert F. during the European War under political commission. Although the European War has long since passed, this gun was only recently completed by Haas. It is estimated that this gun can fire eight hundred 50-pound shells per minute at a distance of nine miles. One person can fire it. The gun body is longer than ordinary gun bodies. Although its form is old, the Navy Department has accepted it, and plans to reward Haas for his efforts. (Yi Kang)

Book and Newspaper Introductions

National Characteristics of Various Countries by Yang Zhijing 200

Written by Zhang Anshi

Published by Huatong Bookstore

(Individuals have personalities, nations have national characteristics.) This is undeniable by anyone. We see the Renaissance, originating in Italy, yet after its spread to various countries, no two are the same. The religious revolution, originating in Germany, also became different in each country after spreading. For example, the modern socialist thought, initially originating from Saint-Simon and Owen, also developed differently in each country. England still only has the trade union movement. The French Socialist Party is slightly more radical. Germany created social democracy, and Russia transformed into the Soviet. After analyzing these in detail using scientific methods, we naturally believe that this is all due to the existence of national character. This is all the result of the integration of the great dominating force of different national characteristics.

Detailed research into various nations and exploration of their historical rise and fall can naturally provide our Chinese nation with a great awakening. The author tells us that there are six common characteristics of declining national characteristics: (1) tepid emotions, (2) weak will, (3) strong individuality but weak restraint, (4) suspicion, (5) imitation, and (6) lack of order. Today, the cruel behavior and cold methods of the Greek, Indian, and Egyptian national characters, their weak will, lack of responsibility, and lack of thoroughness, the division of Indian religious tribal groups, and the suspicious nature of the Greeks, who are called "foxes," all symbolize the decline of national character. Looking back at the current state of our own Chinese national character, undeniable facts tell us that we may have to add two more flaws: "laziness" and "selfishness." Moreover, the majority of the people simply do not understand the glory of fighting for the nation, nor do they have a sense of national consciousness. Looking around at emerging nations such as England, Germany, France, and the United States, "once the country is in trouble, the Conservative Party can cooperate with the Progressive Party, and the Labor Party can work with capitalist groups." What should we think when we see this?

There are indeed very few Chinese scholars who study national character, and even fewer works that study national character. In the long-suffering and decadent Chinese nation, most scholars are probably intoxicated by the environment and have forgotten the so-called nation. The book "National Characteristics of Various Countries" does not dissect the diseased state of the Chinese nation. However, in our Chinese nation, which has long forgotten national consciousness, it can at least provide a stimulus. Comparing the facts of the rise and fall of various national characters, we can see which direction our Chinese nation has been heading in recent times. We are treading on the same path as the decadent national characteristics everywhere. Are we willing to degenerate, or should we brace ourselves and strive for self-determination?

The content of "National Characteristics of Various Countries" is divided into four chapters. In addition to the first and last chapters, which are introductions and conclusions, the second chapter discusses prosperous national characteristics and contains more than twenty-six sections, detailing the national characteristics of Germany, England, America, France, Russia, Italy, and Japan. The third chapter discusses declining national characteristics, with five sections describing the reasons for the decline of the national characteristics of Egypt, Judah, Greece, India, and Spain.

As the author said, "It is very difficult to understand the national characteristics of various countries. First, one must read extensively from various scholars' research on national character. Second, one must travel around various countries and have a deep understanding of the social conditions of each country. Third, one must thoroughly research the spiritual and material aspects of each country." Amidst these many difficulties, the author is even more capable of organizing it systematically using scientific methods and writing it out. We should naturally consider it satisfactory. Before the author studies the characteristics of a nation, he first introduces the natural environment of that country, and then analyzes the historical facts, as well as the cultural environment and overview of thought, in a well-organized manner. While it should not be admitted that the environment has such a great dominating force, and that changes in the environment can also cause races to change accordingly, mentality is influenced by education, and the environment also has considerable power. We naturally cannot absolutely deny it. The author also means this, as he said in the fourth chapter of the introduction, "Based on the scope of research on national character, in addition to heredity, we also emphasize the environment of various national characters, including not only the natural environment but also the social environment."

After reading this book, based on the proof of historical facts, the path our Chinese nation is taking every day is a dead end. We absolutely do not have the common points of emerging national characteristics. We only have the common points of declining national characteristics. Look, "As long as there are three Germans in one place, they will inevitably organize groups." But what is the national character of our Chinese people? Like a sheet of loose sand, "Everyone sweeps the snow from their own door, and doesn't care about the frost on others' roofs," there is absolutely no habit of communal living. Compared with the emerging German national character, it has become an extremely opposite portrayal. Secondly, Germany "during the disturbances of October 1918, the Kiel sailors became independent, and various places responded, even calling for Wilhelm II to abdicate. When the revolution first started, outsiders guessed that Germany would become a second Soviet Russia. But in less than a year, the National Assembly was convened, the constitution was completed, and the political situation was stabilized... still in an orderly manner, without chaotic steps... without following in the footsteps of Soviet Russia. This is entirely an expression of the nation's love for order." And what is the national character of our China? From the beginning of the Republic of China to the present, it has not been able to create a complete constitution, nor has it shown any love for the nation or for order. There has been civil war all year round, only seeing self-abandonment and adding to the symbols of decline.

"The character of our people is to say and not do, the character of the French is to say and then do, the character of the Germans is to do and then say, the character of the British is to do and not say." It is naturally not a bad thing to express opinions as much as possible, but only seeing theoretical articles and never embodying them in reality, what is the benefit? It only provokes people's sneers. This is also a defect of declining national character, which the emerging national characters of France, Germany, and England do not have. The author's judgment is naturally very incisive. (Just look at the "lengthy paper articles" of tens of thousands of words, and the "singing of high-sounding tunes," etc., which are all proofs of the fact of "saying and not doing," while British diplomacy and news are known for their unobtrusive approach.)

"A small island country, with only sixty years of restoration, publicly joins the ranks of the world's great powers. Speaking of military equipment, the army has defeated Russia, and the navy's achievements have surpassed those of France and Italy. Domestic industry, almost everything that Europe and America have, Japan can imitate. This spirit of struggle is naturally worthy of attention... Ancient history says that some people saw the Spartans' diet and said that bad food like that is worse than death, so Spartan warriors emerged. If you have seen the lives of the Japanese, you can understand their struggle." Turning our heads to look at the situation in our country, what a situation it is. Such a large nation has only ended up with backward industries. In a big city, almost everything must be sought from imported goods. Not only is there a lack of willingness to struggle, but there is also extravagance and extreme luxury. Isn't this digging one's own grave?

The most peculiar national character has to be that of Russia, which takes extreme approaches everywhere, but is impermanent. Due to climate and religious reasons, it forms their laziness, but at the same time, it can produce great spirit and become a great nation.

Page 26

, The path that the nation takes, whether it is prosperity or decline, is worthy of people's contemplation. We see in the book that "Russia took the path of an extremely autocratic imperial regime" and turned into communist politics. This change was so rapid that it was as if yesterday there were only rickshaws, and today airships have been discovered. Such an extreme change has almost no second example in history except for Russia. Therefore, the world recognizes Russia as mysterious, and Russians as a mysterious nation. In fact, by studying the Russian national character, one realizes that this extreme change is inherent in Russia and is not surprising at all. It can be seen everywhere in Russian society... even the changes in Soviet Russian politics after the war can prove a lot. For example, at the beginning of the revolution, communism was strictly enforced, the capitalist system was broken, and imperialism was overthrown. But after 1923, it was felt that this path was not feasible, so it was changed to restore the capitalist economy and to associate with imperialists. Since it has restored the capitalist economy, it is also sending people to disturb foreign countries and constantly propagate communism." Looking again at Russia's greatness, "The Russian national character is naturally great. This greatness can be seen in the spirit, in philosophy, in culture, in art, and in architecture, and it can also be seen in politics. For example, when Russia was formerly autocratic, it often aimed at world hegemony and declared when it declared war on Japan that it would open Japan as a world park. This is one example," but it is inevitably too abstract. This is also where the shortcomings of the Russian national character lie.

What will be the path taken by this strange and extremely contradictory Russian national character in the future? What will be the future of the new national movement? The author dare not make a judgment, and it is feared that it is not optimistic.

At the beginning of the chapter on declining national characteristics, the author tells us this: "Declining nations are those that once had civilization, but after a decline, they never recover. Other countries either become strong through revolution or are governed through restoration. Only declining nations not only do not understand revolution and restoration, but even if there are revolutions and restorations, they only help to fuel turmoil." Please look at the situation in our country, is it like this?

A Chinese Enigma by Chunsen 201

Written by Li Qingya

Rainy season and dense fog. With nothing to do in a guest house, I happened to flip through the fourth issue of the first volume of New Literature and Art Magazine, in which the most eye-catching article was Mr. Li Qingya's "A Chinese Enigma."

There are very many Chinese enigmas, but in the eyes of our own people, we think they are ordinary and unremarkable. Unfortunately, in the eyes of foreign races, they are full of surprises and speculations. Therefore, what we ourselves think is unimportant, they on the contrary labor their minds and nerves to care about us, and even take them into their so-called chemical rooms, which they claim are developed by material civilization, or publicize them, saying that there are so many strange things in China. Before the Opium War, China did not sign any commercial treaties with foreigners, so China was still an ancient civilized country in the East, with a seemingly sacred and inviolable dignity, which made the general foreigners respect and obey it. Thus the act of "tribute" occurred. In fact, "speaking of tribute, it was nothing more than a one-sided muddled discussion by those who considered themselves figures of the Celestial Dynasty at the time. In fact, we should at least regard it as a kind of adventurous behavior of those yellow-haired, green-eyed races." What exactly is inside the great ancient country of the East in their ideals is a question they urgently need to solve. Finally, they were willing to compromise, changing bowing to kowtowing, becoming a thing worthy of glory for the Chinese nation. I remember a ridiculous thing, the flow of Chinese silk into the West, which is enough to sigh about. A foreign missionary, because he was afraid that scholars and people from the exporting places would find out, which was not clever, secretly put silkworm seeds in his shoes, so that he could safely deceive them. But now, good silkworm seeds have to be purchased from foreign countries. Isn't this a good story? As for other things, there are too many to count. In short, the secrets of China continue to be an enigma, and it does not matter if they form enigmas in their minds. However, Chinese writers do not seem to have time to care about this enigmatic thing, which is so regrettable and pitiful. Now, thanks to Mr. Li Qingya's initiation, he has relatively revealed a little bit of the glory of our nation, which can also be said to show some color to foreigners. Moreover, we often see Mr. Li Qingya's translations. Creation is very difficult, so this article is even more valuable.

"A Chinese Enigma" is like this. During the Qianlong reign of the Qing Dynasty, a Westerner from some country came to China to pay tribute. At a banquet of entertainment, he tasted "Yuanxiao" (sweet rice balls). That white, round, sweet, and crispy dessert was praised every time he ate it. But they got a strange question, that is, "the dessert they ate in the north was made from a natural fresh fruit that was dried whole," and "determined that even if this dessert was not a natural thing, no one but Confucius could create such a treasure. Furthermore, it is said that only Confucius knew the secret." Later, they questioned again, "How can such a round core be so tightly and evenly wrapped in a deep round shell, without revealing a trace? Chinese toys are really endless enigmas." Finally, after the yamen exhausted all methods and promised to give one hundred taels of silver as a deposit for custom-making two thousand Yuanxiao, a pastry shop was willing to make Yuanxiao for them to see. On the appointed date, they went to the workshop of the shop that claimed to be a follower of Confucius to see the result. After the shopkeeper explained to them one by one, they nodded as if they understood, watching the old craftsman make them. At the same time, they ordered the scientific attendants and doctors to measure the ingredients of each hundred Yuanxiao, how they were matched, and even the weight of that bowl of clear water had to be carefully measured. Before leaving, the minister asked the shopkeeper, "Are you all disciples of Confucius?" The shopkeeper replied, "We dare not climb so high, dare not, dare not, dare not, we only respect Guan Yu and the God of Wealth." Thus, although the diplomat understood why Yuanxiao is Yuanxiao, the enigma of why the pastry shopkeeper dared not climb to be a disciple of Confucius but only respected Guan Yu and the God of Wealth has never been solved. I don't know what the diplomats of the so-called foreign country think now, has it been solved or not?

The author's description of the workshop is so detailed and thorough that I feel like I am there. The actions of those diplomats are also very vivid, revealing all the Chinese enigmas. I hope Mr. Li continues to work hard so that we can read such interesting works, and I also hope that the Chinese literary world will discover more of this kind of work.

After writing these random thoughts, the sound of violent wind blowing through the dense leaves came aggressively, reminding me of the impact the Chinese nation has suffered before and after trade, and I cannot help but feel the past and present.

Overseas Chinese Footprints

Mr. You Gong of the Shanghai Shen Bao received a letter from England, continuing to express his views on Donglian Japan. He was too busy to provide details. He enjoyed the communication very much. Today, Yang Linde and Feng Gensi, along with three other visitors, visited the Sinian Experimental Unlimited Facsimile Telegraph Station. A five-minute telegram can reach Nanjing, which is more convenient than wired facsimile telegrams for long-distance applications. The Primitive Culture of Taiwan's Indigenous Tribes

(1) The Tayal tribe of the Northern Indigenous People reside in the mountainous regions of northern Taiwan. They are fierce and combative, and are the most barbaric. Headhunting is prevalent, and the number of heads taken determines their military merit ranking. However, this practice is gradually declining. Most of the pacification efforts in Taiwan are directed at this tribe, but they are the most stubborn and difficult to subdue.

(2) A photo of the surveyor, Mr. Lin Huixiang, taken with the indigenous people of Lama Bawan Village. When asked to take a photo with the indigenous people, they all wore their clothes, carried knives and guns. The women were unwilling, but after much persuasion, two of them finally agreed. The people squatting in the picture are them.

(3) A type of woven fabric. Garments adorned with ancient grain beads are extremely precious ceremonial attire. Only the elders and the strong were allowed to wear them. This particular garment has as many as sixty thousand grain beads.

(4) Indigenous People's Artwork

Mr. Lin Huixiang of the Ethnology Society of the former Social Science Research Institute of the Academia Sinica in Shanghai went to Taiwan to collect specimens and investigate their way of life. The task has now been completed. The indigenous people of Taiwan, also known as raw aborigines or Gaoshan aborigines, originally belonged to the Malay race. During the Stone Age, they entered Taiwan from Nanyang. Separated from the outside world, isolated from foreign cultures, they largely retained their original culture. The various tribes are a good subject for cultural anthropology. They can be divided into seven major tribes, with a population of about 130,000. They are mainly located in the central mountainous areas and the east coast of Hualien. To this day, they still maintain their traditions. Trade between Taiwanese Han people and indigenous people is limited. Their livelihoods are based on rudimentary agriculture and hunting. The highest level in their social structure is the tribe, followed by the clans and families. Some tribes practice a matriarchal system. The practice of "issuing orders" (headhunting) is used to demonstrate bravery. Ancestor worship is practiced, with some tribes worshiping snakes as their ancestors. Due to the practice of headhunting and snake worship, their knowledge of human origins and snake patterns is extremely basic. Their tattoos, tribal songs, and concepts of numbers and time are all underdeveloped. They cannot record years and have no writing. Mr. Lin's collection includes 143 specimens, divided into weapons, clothing, jewelry, household items, artworks, entertainment items, and record-keeping tools. The Museum of the Governor-General of Taiwan has none of these. The information gained from these specimens is not only useful for understanding the customs of the indigenous people but also reveals the primitive aspects of their civilization. Those who are interested in researching the origins of various human institutions and cultures will find this to be a valuable reference.

(5) The peculiar boats of the Yami tribe. The boats used by the Yami people have high prows and sterns. They are decorated with feathers. The high prows were originally intended to block wind and waves, but now they have become purely decorative. The boat's hull is carved with human figures and various clan symbols.

(6) This is carved from hardwood and is about one foot tall. The hair is arranged in a spiral shape. The carving is rudimentary, and the head is disproportionately small compared to the body. Most of the carved heads depict people who have committed serious crimes. Distinguishing between males and females:

The leather cap decorated with feathers is made of deerskin. A corner is cut off and joined together. It is decorated with bird feathers and supplemented with red patterns. The feathers are from the Taiwanese pheasant bird. It is usually worn during festivals and removed during hunting.

(7) Pottery used by indigenous people. These vessels are about one foot tall, thick and blue in color, decorated with spiral patterns, and have three legs. They are made by hand and fired on flat ground. The spiral patterns resemble snakes and are simple and primitive.

(8) Two indigenous people's dwellings. The houses of the southern indigenous people are more refined than those of the northern indigenous people, but they are still thatched huts. The children standing outside the house wear short, Han-style clothes. The men wear short skirts, and the women wear colorful wide belts. Therefore, the northern indigenous people are more cultured and wealthier.

(9) Indigenous people's dancing. All tribes love to dance even more than civilized people. Taiwan's indigenous tribes are no exception. They only dance during festivals and gatherings. The most popular dance is the circle dance, as shown in the picture above. The dancers carry poles and chant in unison, harmonizing rhythmically.

(10) Indigenous people's customs. Indigenous men are all warriors. From a young age, they practice climbing mountains, wading through rivers, and skills such as stealth and concealment. Their movements are very agile. They have been using knives and spears for centuries. Only in recent years have they learned to use guns from the Han people. They are extremely skilled in shooting, which is admired by the Han people and the Japanese.

(11 12 13) Relics from the Stone Age. Shaped like a plate and short and wide, with a beveled edge and one side perpendicular. They are used to be held in the hand to scrape and peel animal skins and wood. The stone material is very hard. Many of these have been found.

(1) Raising Birds In the early morning, holding a bird on a short string near a lush grove of trees, the birds begin to sing, responding to each other with melodious sounds like music. The person in the picture is Ms. Yang Xiuying.

(2) Talking About the Long Summer Sitting on a mat by the water with close friends, discussing ancient and modern times, the most effective way to pass the long summer. (C)

(3) Listening to Cicadas Sitting in the shade of a willow tree in the afternoon, listening to the sound of cicadas high in the trees, makes one's mind calm and the mood peaceful, dispelling all worries. The person in the picture is Ms. Zhang Naomo (Song Ji)

(4) Testing the Breeze In the faint light of dawn, going to the suburbs to test the direction of the wind, one almost forgets that it is the height of summer. After returning home for a bath, one feels doubly refreshed. The person in the picture is Ms. Zhou Yingxia.

(5) Bathing a Child Children are naturally active and sweat easily. In the summer, it is especially important for mothers to bathe them frequently. The person in the picture is Ms. Liu Shen Shuyun. (M)

(6) Playing Billiards The capital lacks high-end entertainment venues, but the International Recreation Club has billiards tables, which are sufficient for spending leisure time during the long summer. The person in the picture is Dr. Wang Qiaotang. (L)

(7) Three Terrace Cave, Yanziji, Nanjing Usually, it is very popular, but during the day, there is sunlight shining through. Walking through it, one feels a chilling darkness. (Jin Huating)

(8) Playing the Piano Playing a dreamy tune among the green trees as the sun sets makes one feel clear-headed and distant. The person in the picture is Ms. Li Suhua.

(9) Showering In the Hongkou Swimming Pool, next to the shallow water, there are sprinklers that spray water like a heavy rain. Swimmers often enjoy showering under them. (Lin Zemin)
